<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the country. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Haiti_(disambiguation)" title="Haiti (disambiguation)">Haiti (disambiguation)</a>. "Hayti" and "Ayiti" redirect here. For the island of Haiti, see <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>.</div>

<div style="padding-bottom:0.3em;"><span lang="fr">"<a href="/wiki/Libert%C3%A9,_%C3%A9galit%C3%A9,_fraternit%C3%A9" title="Liberté, égalité, fraternité">Liberté, égalité, fraternité</a>"</span> <span class="languageicon" style="font-size:81%;font-weight:normal;">(French)</span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><br/>

<p><b>Haiti</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'h' in 'hi'">h</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/iː/ or /ɪ/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Haiti.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bb/En-us-Haiti.ogg" title="En-us-Haiti.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <span lang="fr"><i>Haïti</i></span> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[a.iti]</a></span>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole_language" title="Haitian Creole language">Haitian Creole</a>: <span lang="ht"><i>Ayiti</i></span> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Haitian_Creole" title="Help:IPA/Haitian Creole">[ajiti]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Haiti</b> (French: <span lang="fr"><i>République d'Haïti</i></span>; Haitian Creole: <span lang="ht"><i>Repiblik Ayiti</i></span>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> and formerly called <b>Hayti</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[note 1]</a></sup> is a country located on the island of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a> archipelago of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>. It occupies the western three-eighths of the island, which it shares with the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dardik_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dardik-12">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Current_Affairs_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Current_Affairs-13">[12]</a></sup> Haiti is 27,750 square kilometres (10,714 sq mi) in size and has an estimated 10.8 million people,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">[3]</a></sup> making it the most populous country in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community</a> (CARICOM) and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Caribbean_island_countries_by_population" title="List of Caribbean island countries by population">second-most populous</a> country in the Caribbean as a whole.</p>
<p>The region was originally inhabited by the indigenous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" title="Taíno people">Taíno people</a>. Spain discovered the island on 5 December 1492 during the <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus#First_voyage" title="Christopher Columbus">first voyage</a> of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> across the Atlantic. When Columbus initially landed in Haiti, he had thought he had found <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> or <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NgCheong-Lum.2C_Roseline_19_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-NgCheong-Lum.2C_Roseline_19-14">[13]</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas Day</a> 1492, Columbus' flagship the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_(ship)" title="Santa Maria (ship)">Santa Maria</a></i> ran aground north of what is now <a href="/wiki/Limonade" title="Limonade">Limonade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davies1953_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davies1953-15">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> As a consequence, Columbus ordered his men to salvage what they could from the ship, and he created the first European settlement in the Americas, naming it <a href="/wiki/La_Navidad" title="La Navidad">La Navidad</a> after the day the ship was destroyed.</p>
<p>The island was named <i>La Española</i> and claimed by <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spain</a>, which ruled until the early 17th century. Competing claims and settlements by the French led to the western portion of the island being <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Ryswick" title="Treaty of Ryswick">ceded to France</a>, which named it <i>Saint-Domingue</i>. <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">Sugarcane</a> <a href="/wiki/Sugar_plantations_in_the_Caribbean" title="Sugar plantations in the Caribbean">plantations</a>, worked by slaves brought from Africa, were established by colonists.</p>
<p>In the midst of the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> (1789–1799), slaves and <a href="/wiki/Gens_de_couleur" title="Gens de couleur">free people of colour</a> revolted in the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">Haitian Revolution</a> (1791–1804), culminating in the abolition of slavery and the defeat of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon Bonaparte</a>'s army at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Verti%C3%A8res" title="Battle of Vertières">Battle of Vertières</a>. Afterward the sovereign nation of Haiti was established on 1 January 1804 –  the first independent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nation-state" title="Nation-state">nation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, the second <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> in the Americas, the only nation in the western hemisphere to have defeated three European <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpowers</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">France</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Spain" title="Imperial Spain">Spain</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">UK</a>), and the only nation in the world established as a result of a successful <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_revolt" title="Slave revolt">slave revolt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> The rebellion that began in 1791 was led by a former slave and the first black general of the <a href="/wiki/French_Army" title="French Army">French Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toussaint_Louverture" title="Toussaint Louverture">Toussaint Louverture</a>, whose military genius and political acumen transformed an entire society of <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slaves</a> into an independent country. Upon his death in a prison in France, he was succeeded by his lieutenant, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Dessalines" title="Jean-Jacques Dessalines">Jean-Jacques Dessalines</a>, who declared Haiti's <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> and later became the first Emperor of Haiti, <i>Jacques I</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">Haitian Revolution</a> lasted just over a dozen years; and apart from <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_P%C3%A9tion" title="Alexandre Pétion">Alexandre Pétion</a>, the first President of the Republic, all the first leaders of government were former slaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re" title="Citadelle Laferrière">Citadelle Laferrière</a> is the largest fortress in the Americas. <a href="/wiki/Henri_Christophe" title="Henri Christophe">Henri Christophe</a> –  former slave and first king of Haiti, <i>Henri I</i> –  built it to withstand a possible foreign attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.google.com_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-news.google.com-27">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>It is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a> (OAS),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Caribbean_States" title="Association of Caribbean States">Association of Caribbean States</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">International Francophonie Organisation</a>. In addition to CARICOM, it is a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_States" title="Community of Latin American and Caribbean States">Community of Latin American and Caribbean States</a>. It has the lowest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> in the Americas. Most recently, in February 2004, a <i><a href="/wiki/2004_Haitian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2004 Haitian coup d'état">coup d'état</a></i> originating in the north of the country forced the resignation and exile of President <a href="/wiki/Jean-Bertrand_Aristide" title="Jean-Bertrand Aristide">Jean-Bertrand Aristide</a>. A provisional government took control with security provided by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Stabilization_Mission_in_Haiti" title="United Nations Stabilization Mission in Haiti">United Nations Stabilization Mission in Haiti</a> (MINUSTAH).</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The name Haiti (or <i>Hayti</i>) comes from the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">Taíno</a> language which was the native name<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[note 2]</a></sup> given to the entire island of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> to mean, "land of high mountains."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup> The <i>h</i> is silent in French and the <i><a href="/wiki/%C3%8F" title="Ï">ï</a></i> in <i>Ha<b>ï</b>ti</i>, is a <a href="/wiki/Diaeresis_(diacritic)#French" title="Diaeresis (diacritic)">diacritical mark</a> used to show that the second vowel is pronounced separately, as in the word <i>na<b>ï</b>ve</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> In English, this rule for the pronunciation is often disregarded, thus the spelling <i>Haiti</i> is used. There are different anglicizations for its pronunciation such as HIGH-ti, high-EE-ti and haa-EE-ti, which are still in use, but <i>HAY-ti</i> is the most widespread and established.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The name was restored by Haitian revolutionary Jean-Jacques Dessalines as the official name of independent Saint-Domingue, as a tribute to the Amerindian predecessors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>In French, Haiti's nickname is the <i>Pearl of the Antilles</i> (<i>La Perle des Antilles</i>) because of both its natural beauty,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> and the amount of wealth it accumulated for the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">Kingdom of France</a>, as it was considered the richest colony owned by any of the European powers at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Haiti" title="History of Haiti">History of Haiti</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian_history">Pre-Columbian history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-Columbian history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Chiefdoms_of_Hispaniola" title="Chiefdoms of Hispaniola">Chiefdoms of Hispaniola</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1171" data-file-width="2341" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png/350px-Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png/525px-Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png/700px-Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Copia_de_Cacicazgos_de_la_Hispaniola.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The five <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">caciquedoms</a> of Hispaniola at the time of the arrival of Christopher Columbus</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the time of European encounter, the island of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>, of which Haiti occupies the western three-eighths,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dardik_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dardik-12">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Current_Affairs_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Current_Affairs-13">[12]</a></sup> was one of many Caribbean islands inhabited by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" title="Taíno people">Taíno</a> Indians, speakers of an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arawakan" title="Arawakan">Arawakan</a> language called Taino, which has been preserved in the Haitian Creole language. The Taíno name for the entire island was <i>Haiti</i>. The people had migrated over centuries into the Caribbean islands from South America. Genetic studies show they were related to the <a href="/wiki/Yanomami" title="Yanomami">Yanomami</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_Basin" title="Amazon Basin">Amazon Basin</a>. They also originated in Central and South America. After migrating to Caribbean islands, in the 15th century, the Taíno were pushed into the northeast Caribbean islands by the <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">Caribs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-royal_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-royal-42">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the Taíno societies of the Caribbean islands, the largest unit of political organization was led by a <i><a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">cacique</a>,</i> or chief, as the Europeans understood them. The island of Haiti was divided among five Caciquats: the Magua in the north east, the Marien in the north west, the Xaragua in the south west, the Maguana in the center region of Cibao and the Higuey in the south east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup> The caciquedoms were tributary kingdoms, with payment consisting of harvests.</p>
<p>Taíno cultural artifacts include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cave_paintings" title="Cave paintings">cave paintings</a> in several locations in the country. These have become national symbols of Haiti and tourist attractions. Modern-day <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%C3%A9ogane" title="Léogane">Léogane</a> started as a French colonial town in the southwest, is beside the former capital of the caciquedom of <i>Xaragua.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-royal_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-royal-42">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Spanish_rule_(1492–1625)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_rule_.281492.E2.80.931625.29">Spanish rule (1492–1625)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Spanish rule (1492–1625)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="693" data-file-width="816" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg/220px-Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg/330px-Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg/440px-Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_landing_on_Hispaniola_adj.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Christopher Columbus landing on Hispaniola</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Piktograf1.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="304" data-file-width="400" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Piktograf1.png/220px-Piktograf1.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Piktograf1.png/330px-Piktograf1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bb/Piktograf1.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Piktograf1.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1510 Taíno <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pictograph" title="Pictograph">pictograph</a> telling a story of missionaries arriving in <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Navigator <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> landed in Haiti on 5 December 1492, in an area that he named <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%B4le_Saint-Nicolas" title="Môle Saint-Nicolas">Môle Saint-Nicolas</a>,</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup> and claimed the island for the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a>. Nineteen days later, his ship the <i><a href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_(ship)" title="Santa María (ship)">Santa María</a></i> ran aground near the present site of <a href="/wiki/Cap-Ha%C3%AFtien" title="Cap-Haïtien">Cap-Haïtien</a>. Columbus left 39 men on the island, who founded the settlement of <a href="/wiki/La_Navidad" title="La Navidad">La Navidad</a>.</p>
<p>The sailors carried <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endemic" title="Endemic">endemic</a> <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasian</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infectious_disease" title="Infectious disease">infectious diseases</a>. The natives lacked <a href="/wiki/Immunity_(medical)" title="Immunity (medical)">immunity</a> to these new diseases and died in great numbers in <a href="/wiki/Epidemic" title="Epidemic">epidemics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> The first recorded <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> epidemic in the Americas erupted on Hispaniola in 1507.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> The <i><span lang="es"><a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">encomienda</a></span></i> system forced natives to work in gold mines and plantations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Spanish passed the <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_Burgos" title="Laws of Burgos">Laws of Burgos, 1512–13</a>, which forbade the maltreatment of natives, endorsed their <a href="/wiki/Proselytism" title="Proselytism">conversion</a> to Catholicism,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> and gave legal framework to <i><span lang="es">encomiendas</span>.</i> The natives were brought to these sites to work in specific plantations or industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a gateway to the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> became a haven for <a href="/wiki/Piracy_in_the_Caribbean" title="Piracy in the Caribbean">pirates</a> during the early colonial period. The western part of the island was settled by French <a href="/wiki/Buccaneer" title="Buccaneer">buccaneers</a>. Among them was Bertrand d'Ogeron, who succeeded in growing <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a>. He recruited many French colonial families from <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>. European nations were competing for control in the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> as well as in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">France</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Spain" title="Imperial Spain">Spain</a> settled their hostilities on the island, by way of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Ryswick" title="Treaty of Ryswick">Treaty of Ryswick</a> of 1697, and divided Hispaniola between them.</p>
<h3><span id="French_rule_(1625–1804)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="French_rule_.281625.E2.80.931804.29">French rule (1625–1804)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: French rule (1625–1804)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a></div>
<p>France received the western third and subsequently named it <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a>, the French equivalent of <i><a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Santo_Domingo" title="Captaincy General of Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a></i>, the Spanish colony of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> and the name of its patron saint, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Dominic" title="Saint Dominic">Saint Dominic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstcolony_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-firstcolony-52">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>To develop it into sugarcane plantations, the French imported thousands of slaves from <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>. Sugar was a lucrative <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commodity_crop" title="Commodity crop">commodity crop</a> throughout the 18th century. By 1789, approximately 40,000 white colonists lived in Saint-Domingue. In contrast, by 1763 the white population of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">French Canada</a>, a vast territory, had numbered 65,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> The whites were vastly outnumbered by the tens of thousands of African slaves they had imported to work on their plantations, which were primarily devoted to the production of sugarcane. In the north of the island, slaves were able to retain many ties to African cultures, religion and language; these ties were continually being renewed by newly imported Africans. Blacks outnumbered whites by about ten to one.</p>
<p>The French-enacted <i><a href="/wiki/Code_Noir" title="Code Noir">Code Noir</a></i> ("Black Code"), prepared by <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Colbert" title="Jean-Baptiste Colbert">Jean-Baptiste Colbert</a> and ratified by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_XIV" title="Louis XIV">Louis XIV</a>, had established rules on slave treatment and permissible freedoms. Saint-Domingue has been described as one of the most brutally efficient slave colonies; one-third of newly imported Africans died within a few years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Farmer-LROB_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Farmer-LROB-54">[52]</a></sup> Many slaves died from diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Typhoid_fever" title="Typhoid fever">typhoid fever</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> They had low <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rates</a>, and there is evidence that some women <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">aborted</a> fetuses rather than give birth to children within the bonds of slavery.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>As in its <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">Louisiana colony</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">French colonial</a> government allowed some rights to <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free people of color</a>: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed-race" title="Mixed-race">mixed-race</a> descendants of white male colonists and black female slaves (and later, mixed-race women). Over time, many were released from slavery. They established a separate <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">social class</a>. White French <a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples" title="Creole peoples">Creole</a> fathers frequently sent their mixed-race sons to <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> for their education. Some men of color were admitted into the military. More of the free people of color lived in the south of the island, near <a href="/wiki/Port-au-Prince" title="Port-au-Prince">Port-au-Prince</a>, and many intermarried within their community. They frequently worked as artisans and tradesmen, and began to own some property. Some became slave holders. The <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free people of color</a> petitioned the <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">colonial</a> government to expand their rights.</p>
<p>Slaves that made it to Haiti from the trans-Atlantic journey and slaves born in Haiti were first documented in Haiti's archives and transferred to France's Ministry of Defense and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, these records are in The National Archives of France. According to the 1788 Census, Haiti's population consisted of nearly 25,000 whites, 22,000 free coloureds and 700,000 slaves.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span id="Haitian_Revolution_(1791–1804)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Haitian_Revolution_.281791.E2.80.931804.29">Haitian Revolution (1791–1804)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Haitian Revolution (1791–1804)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">Haitian Revolution</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Frontispiece_from_the_book_Saint-Domingue,_ou_Histoire_de_Ses_R%C3%A9volutions._ca._1815_(colorcopy).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="429" data-file-width="734" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Frontispiece_from_the_book_Saint-Domingue%2C_ou_Histoire_de_Ses_R%C3%A9volutions._ca._1815_%28colorcopy%29.jpg/220px-Frontispiece_from_the_book_Saint-Domingue%2C_ou_Histoire_de_Ses_R%C3%A9volutions._ca._1815_%28colorcopy%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Frontispiece_from_the_book_Saint-Domingue%2C_ou_Histoire_de_Ses_R%C3%A9volutions._ca._1815_%28colorcopy%29.jpg/330px-Frontispiece_from_the_book_Saint-Domingue%2C_ou_Histoire_de_Ses_R%C3%A9volutions._ca._1815_%28colorcopy%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Frontispiece_from_the_book_Saint-Domingue%2C_ou_Histoire_de_Ses_R%C3%A9volutions._ca._1815_%28colorcopy%29.jpg/440px-Frontispiece_from_the_book_Saint-Domingue%2C_ou_Histoire_de_Ses_R%C3%A9volutions._ca._1815_%28colorcopy%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Frontispiece_from_the_book_Saint-Domingue,_ou_Histoire_de_Ses_R%C3%A9volutions._ca._1815_(colorcopy).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Burning of the town of <a href="/wiki/Cap-Ha%C3%AFtien" title="Cap-Haïtien">Cap-Français</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1815</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="760" data-file-width="457" height="366" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg/220px-G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg/330px-G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg/440px-G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:G%C3%A9n%C3%A9ral_Toussaint_Louverture.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
General <a href="/wiki/Toussaint_Louverture" title="Toussaint Louverture">Toussaint Louverture</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Inspired by the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> of 1789 and principles of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rights_of_man" title="Rights of man">rights of man</a>, <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free people of color</a> and slaves in <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a> and the <a href="/wiki/French_West_Indies" title="French West Indies">French West Indies</a> pressed for freedom and more <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_rights" title="Civil rights">civil rights</a>. Most important was the revolution of the slaves in Saint-Domingue, starting in the northern plains in 1791, where Africans greatly outnumbered the whites.</p>
<p>In 1792, the <a href="/wiki/French_First_Republic" title="French First Republic">French</a> government sent three commissioners with troops to re-establish control. To build an alliance with the <i><a href="/wiki/Gens_de_couleur" title="Gens de couleur">gens de couleur</a></i> and slaves, the French commissioners <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sonthonax" title="Sonthonax">Sonthonax</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polverel" title="Polverel">Polverel</a> abolished slavery in the colony. Six months later, the <a href="/wiki/National_Convention" title="National Convention">National Convention</a>, led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robespierre" title="Robespierre">Robespierre</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacobin_Club" title="Jacobin Club">Jacobins</a>, endorsed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abolition_of_slavery_timeline" title="Abolition of slavery timeline">abolition</a> and extended it to all the French colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Political leaders in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, which was a new republic itself, reacted with ambivalence, at times providing aid to enable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planter_(plantation_owner)" title="Planter (plantation owner)">planters</a> to put down the revolt. Later in the revolution, the US provided support to black Haitian military forces, with the goal of reducing French influence in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Toussaint_Louverture" title="Toussaint Louverture">Toussaint Louverture</a>, a former slave and leader in the slave revolt, drove out the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish</a> (from Santo Domingo) and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">British</a> invaders who threatened the colony. In the uncertain years of revolution, the United States played both sides off against each other, with its traders supplying both the French and the rebels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup> The struggle within Haiti between the <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free people of color</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Rigaud" title="André Rigaud">André Rigaud</a> and the black Haitians led by Louverture devolved into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_of_the_Knives" title="War of the Knives">War of the Knives</a> in 1799 and 1800.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> Many surviving free people of color left the island as refugees.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="642" data-file-width="800" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg/220px-Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg/330px-Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg/440px-Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_for_Palm_Tree_Hill.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Battle between <a href="/wiki/Polish_Legions_(Napoleonic_period)" title="Polish Legions (Napoleonic period)">Polish troops</a> in French service and the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">Haitian rebels</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After Louverture created a separatist constitution, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_French_Republic" title="First French Republic">Napoléon Bonaparte</a> in 1802 sent an expedition of 20,000 soldiers and as many sailors<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup> under the command of his brother-in-law, General <a href="/wiki/Charles_Leclerc" title="Charles Leclerc">Charles Leclerc</a>, to retake the island. The French achieved some victories, but within a few months, most of the <a href="/wiki/French_Army" title="French Army">French</a> had died from <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">yellow fever</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> More than 50,000 French troops died in an attempt to retake the colony, including 18 generals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> The French captured Louverture, transporting him to France for trial. He was imprisoned at <a href="/wiki/Fort_de_Joux" title="Fort de Joux">Fort de Joux</a>, where he died in 1803 of exposure and possibly <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Farmer-LROB_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-Farmer-LROB-54">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>The slaves, along with free <i>gens de couleur</i> and allies, continued their fight for independence. <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Dessalines" title="Jean-Jacques Dessalines">Jean-Jacques Dessalines</a> defeated French troops at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Verti%C3%A8res" title="Battle of Vertières">Battle of Vertières</a> on 18 November 1803, leading the first ever successful slave army revolution. In late 1803, France withdrew its remaining 7,000 troops from the island and Napoleon gave up his idea of re-establishing a <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North American</a> empire. With the war going badly, he sold <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">Louisiana (New France)</a> to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana Purchase</a>.</p>
<h3><span id="First_Empire_(1804–1806)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Empire_.281804.E2.80.931806.29">First Empire (1804–1806)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: First Empire (1804–1806)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/First_Empire_of_Haiti" title="First Empire of Haiti">First Empire of Haiti</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1804_Haiti_Massacre" title="1804 Haiti Massacre">1804 Haiti Massacre</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Le_serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="441" height="324" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Le_serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres.jpg/220px-Le_serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Le_serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres.jpg/330px-Le_serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Le_serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres.jpg/440px-Le_serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Le_serment_des_Anc%C3%AAtres.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pétion and Dessalines swearing allegiance to each other before God; painting by <a href="/wiki/Guillaume_Guillon-Lethi%C3%A8re" title="Guillaume Guillon-Lethière">Guillon-Lethière</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The independence of Saint-Domingue was proclaimed by Dessalines on 1 January 1804.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-64">[62]</a></sup> The exact number of deaths due to the Haitian Revolution is unknown.</p>
<p>Dessalines was proclaimed "Emperor for Life" by his troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> Dessalines at first offered protection to the white planters and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> Once in power, he ordered the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1804_Haiti_Massacre" title="1804 Haiti Massacre">massacre</a> of most whites. Without regard to age or gender, those who did not swear allegiance to him were slain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davies2008_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davies2008-67">[65]</a></sup> In the continuing competition for power, he was assassinated by rivals on 17 October 1806.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haiti_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Haiti-68">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Only <a href="/wiki/1804_Haiti_massacre#Aftermath" title="1804 Haiti massacre">three categories of white people</a> were selected out as exceptions and spared: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_Haitian" title="Polish Haitian">Polish</a> soldiers, the majority of whom deserted from the French army and fought alongside the Haitian rebels; the little group of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Haitian" title="German Haitian">German</a> colonists invited to the <a href="/wiki/Nord-Ouest_(department)" title="Nord-Ouest (department)">north-west region</a>; and a group of <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">medical doctors</a> and professionals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> Reportedly, people with connections to officers in the Haitian army were also spared, as well as the women who agreed to marry non-white men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fearful of the influence of the slaves' revolution, U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a> refused to recognize the new republic, as did most European nations. The U.S. did not officially recognize Haiti for decades, until after the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>The revolution led to a wave of emigration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup> In 1809, nearly 10,000 refugees from Saint-Domingue settled <i>en masse</i> in <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> They doubled the city's population. In addition, the newly arrived slaves added to the city's African population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="State_of_Haiti,_Kingdom_of_Haiti_and_the_Republic_(1806–1820)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="State_of_Haiti.2C_Kingdom_of_Haiti_and_the_Republic_.281806.E2.80.931820.29">State of Haiti, Kingdom of Haiti and the Republic (1806–1820)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: State of Haiti, Kingdom of Haiti and the Republic (1806–1820)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/State_of_Haiti" title="State of Haiti">State of Haiti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Haiti" title="Kingdom of Haiti">Kingdom of Haiti</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>

</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2015" data-file-width="3022" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg/220px-Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg/330px-Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg/440px-Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re_Aerial_View.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Citadelle_Laferri%C3%A8re" title="Citadelle Laferrière">Citadelle Laferrière</a> is the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fortress" title="Fortress">fortress</a> in the Americas, and is considered locally to be the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eighth_wonder_of_the_world" title="Eighth wonder of the world">eighth wonder of the world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.google.com_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-news.google.com-27">[26]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Saint-Domingue was divided between the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Haiti" title="Kingdom of Haiti">Kingdom of Haiti</a> in the north, directed by Henri Christophe, who declared himself <a href="/wiki/Henri_Christophe" title="Henri Christophe">Henri I</a>, and a republic in the south, directed by <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_P%C3%A9tion" title="Alexandre Pétion">Alexandre Pétion</a>, an <i>homme de couleur</i>. Henri Christophe established a semi-feudal <a href="/wiki/Corv%C3%A9e" title="Corvée">corvée</a> system, with a rigid education and economic code.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (July 2013)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>President Pétion gave military and financial assistance to the revolutionary leader <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a>, which were critical in enabling him to liberate the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of New Granada">Viceroyalty of New Granada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> He was instrumental in aiding countries in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> achieve independence from <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">Spain</a>.</p>
<h3><span id="Haitian_unification_(1821–1844)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Haitian_unification_.281821.E2.80.931844.29">Haitian unification (1821–1844)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Haitian unification (1821–1844)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Hispaniola" title="Unification of Hispaniola">Unification of Hispaniola</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_(Hispaniola_Unification_Regime)_Portrait.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="460" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg/180px-President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg/270px-President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg/360px-President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_%28Hispaniola_Unification_Regime%29_Portrait.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:President_Jean-Pierre_Boyer_of_Haiti_(Hispaniola_Unification_Regime)_Portrait.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Boyer" title="Jean-Pierre Boyer">Jean-Pierre Boyer</a> the mulatto ruler of Haiti.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beginning in 1821, President <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Boyer" title="Jean-Pierre Boyer">Jean-Pierre Boyer</a>, also an <i>homme de couleur</i> and successor to Pétion, reunified the two parts of Haiti and extended control over the entire western portion of the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup> In addition, after <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a> declared its independence from Spain on 30 November 1821, Boyer sent <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Hispaniola" title="Unification of Hispaniola">forces in to take control</a>. Boyer ruled the entire island with iron rule, ending slavery in Santo Domingo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> After Santo Domingo achieved independence from Haiti, it established a separate national identity.</p>
<p>Struggling to revive the agricultural economy to produce <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commodity_crops" title="Commodity crops">commodity crops</a>, Boyer passed the Code Rural, which denied peasant laborers the right to leave the land, enter the towns, or start farms or shops of their own. Following the Revolution, many peasants wanted to have their own farms rather than work on plantations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Colonization_Society" title="American Colonization Society">American Colonization Society</a> (ACS) encouraged <a href="/wiki/Free_negro" title="Free negro">free blacks</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> to emigrate to Haiti. Starting in September 1824, more than 6,000 <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">African Americans</a> migrated to Haiti, with transportation paid by the ACS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> Many found the conditions too harsh and returned to the United States.</p>
<p>In July 1825, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_X" title="Charles X">King Charles X</a> of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, during a period of restoration of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_monarchy" title="French monarchy">monarchy</a>, sent a <a href="/wiki/French_Navy" title="French Navy">fleet</a> to reconquer the island. Under pressure, <a href="/wiki/Haiti_indemnity_controversy" title="Haiti indemnity controversy">President Boyer agreed to a treaty</a> by which France formally recognized the independence of the nation in exchange for a payment of 150 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francs" title="Francs">francs</a> (reduced to 90 million in 1838). The Haitian president would have had little choice as the country, unknowingly to him, would have been blockaded by French ships if the exchange did not go the French way. After losing the support of Haiti's elite, Boyer was ousted in 1843. A long succession of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coup" title="Coup">coups</a> followed his departure to exile.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Claiming something without evidence (June 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>The enforced payment to France reduced Haiti's economy for years. Western nations did not give Haiti formal <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomatic</a> recognition. Both of these problems kept the Haitian economy and society isolated. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Expatriates" title="Expatriates">Expatriates</a> bankrolled and armed opposing groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UOH_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-UOH-83">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Second_Empire_(1849–1859)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Empire_.281849.E2.80.931859.29">Second Empire (1849–1859)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Second Empire (1849–1859)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Second_Empire_of_Haiti" title="Second Empire of Haiti">Second Empire of Haiti</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
