</table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_20th_century">Early 20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Early 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_occupation_of_Haiti" title="United States occupation of Haiti">United States occupation of Haiti</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Luders_Affair,_Germany,_Haiti.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="586" data-file-width="882" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Luders_Affair%2C_Germany%2C_Haiti.jpg/220px-Luders_Affair%2C_Germany%2C_Haiti.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Luders_Affair%2C_Germany%2C_Haiti.jpg/330px-Luders_Affair%2C_Germany%2C_Haiti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Luders_Affair%2C_Germany%2C_Haiti.jpg/440px-Luders_Affair%2C_Germany%2C_Haiti.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Luders_Affair,_Germany,_Haiti.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German Captain Thiele of the <i>Charlotte</i> handing over the German Ultimatum on 6 December 1897 during the Luders Affair</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti,_circa_1919.,_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2599" data-file-width="3000" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti%2C_circa_1919.%2C_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif/lossy-page1-235px-U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti%2C_circa_1919.%2C_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti%2C_circa_1919.%2C_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif/lossy-page1-353px-U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti%2C_circa_1919.%2C_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti%2C_circa_1919.%2C_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif/lossy-page1-470px-U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti%2C_circa_1919.%2C_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif.jpg 2x" width="235"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:U.S._Marines_and_guide_in_search_of_bandits._Haiti,_circa_1919.,_1927_-_1981_-_NARA_-_532584.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">US Marines</a> and guide in search of bandits, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">  1919</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1892, the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German government</a> supported suppression of the reform movement of <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%A9nor_Firmin" title="Anténor Firmin">Anténor Firmin</a> and in 1897 the Germans used <a href="/wiki/Gunboat_diplomacy" title="Gunboat diplomacy">gunboat diplomacy</a> to intimidate and then humiliate the Haitian government during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luders_Affair" title="Luders Affair">Luders Affair</a>.</p>
<p>In the first decades of the 20th century Haiti experienced great political instability and was heavily in debt to France, Germany and the United States. Fearing possible foreign intervention, President Woodrow Wilson sent U.S. Marines into Haiti in December 1914, just after the outbreak of World War I. They removed $500,000 from the Haitian National Bank for "safe-keeping" (sic) in New York, thus giving the United States control of the bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an expression of the <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore</a> <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Corollary" title="Roosevelt Corollary">Roosevelt Corollary</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Monroe_Doctrine" title="Monroe Doctrine">Monroe Doctrine</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_occupation_of_Haiti" title="United States occupation of Haiti">United States occupied</a> the island in July 1915 after the assassination of Haiti's president, Vilbrun Guillaume Sam. The pro-American President had been dragged from the French legation and killed in the street by local insurgents after he had ordered 167 political prisoners killed. <a href="/wiki/USS_Washington_(ACR-11)" title="USS Washington (ACR-11)">USS <i>Washington</i></a>, under Rear Admiral <a href="/wiki/William_Banks_Caperton" title="William Banks Caperton">Caperton</a>, arrived in Port-au-Prince to try to restore order and protect American interests. This began a nearly 20-year occupation by U.S. forces. Within days, the Marines had taken control of the capital city and its banks and customs house which controlled all the finances of the island nation. The Marines declared martial law and severely censored the press. Within weeks a new pro-American President, <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Sudr%C3%A9_Dartiguenave" title="Philippe Sudré Dartiguenave">Philippe Sudré Dartiguenave</a>, had been installed and a new constitution written that was favorable to the interests of the United States. The new constitution included a clause that allowed, for the first time, foreign ownership of land in Haiti, which was bitterly opposed by the Haitian legislature and citizenry.</p>
<p>The next 5 years witnessed numerous cases of intimidation, arson, torture and murder of the Haitian population by U.S. Marines and their local enforcers, the Gendarmerie d'Haiti. The U.S. Marines were instilled with a special brand of paternalism allowing them to behave this way. Mary Renda writes that "paternalism was an assertion of authority, superiority, and control expressed in the metaphor of a father's relationship with his children."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup> This mindset allowed the marines to act highly authoritatively in Haiti and carry out atrocious acts. It has been estimated that up to 15,000 Haitians lost their lives at the hands of the occupying forces, either through armed opposition or through the 'corvee' system of forced labor. This system allowed the occupying forces to take people from their homes and farms, at gunpoint if necessary, to build roads, bridges, etc. Many resisted and were killed on the spot while others died working or due to disease and malnutrition while living in squalid work camps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>This chapter in the two nations' histories reflects the oppressive foreign policy of the United States toward its neighbors in Central America and the Caribbean that is often characterized as "<a href="/wiki/Gunboat_diplomacy" title="Gunboat diplomacy">gunboat diplomacy</a>" or one of many "<a href="/wiki/Banana_Wars" title="Banana Wars">Banana Wars</a>" that plagued the region in the early 20th century. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Marines" title="U.S. Marines">U.S. Marines</a> were stationed in the country until 1934, a period of nineteen years, and were finally ordered from the island by Franklin D. Roosevelt as a demonstration of his "Good Neighbor Policy". However, the United States controlled the economy of the island and heavily influenced elections in Haiti up through the 1980s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sisal" title="Sisal">Sisal</a> was introduced to Haiti, and sugarcane and <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> became significant exports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Henl.2C_pp._454.E2.80.93455_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Henl.2C_pp._454.E2.80.93455-87">[85]</a></sup> Haitian traditionalists, based in rural areas, were highly resistant to <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a>-backed changes, while the urban elites wanted more control. Together they helped secure an end to the occupation in 1934.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> The debts were still outstanding and the American financial advisor-general receiver handled the budget until 1941.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Recognition of the distinctive traditionalism of the Haitian people had an influence on United States writers, including <a href="/wiki/Eugene_O%27Neill" title="Eugene O'Neill">Eugene O'Neill</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Weldon_Johnson" title="James Weldon Johnson">James Weldon Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Langston_Hughes" title="Langston Hughes">Langston Hughes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zora_Neale_Hurston" title="Zora Neale Hurston">Zora Neale Hurston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orson_Welles" title="Orson Welles">Orson Welles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>After US forces left in 1934, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican</a> dictator <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Trujillo" title="Rafael Trujillo">Rafael Trujillo</a> used <a href="/wiki/Antihaitianismo" title="Antihaitianismo">anti-Haitian</a> sentiment as a nationalist tool. In an event that became known as the <a href="/wiki/Parsley_massacre" title="Parsley massacre">Parsley massacre</a>, he ordered his Army to kill Haitians living on the Dominican side of the border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Farmer180_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Farmer180-91">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wucker_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-wucker-92">[90]</a></sup> Between 10,000 and 20,000 Haitians were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Farmer180_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-Farmer180-91">[89]</a></sup> Though he was one-quarter Haitian himself, Trujillo continued policies against the neighboring population for some time.</p>
<p>On 27 September 1945,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup> Haiti became a <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">founding member</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (successor to the <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_League_of_Nations" title="Member states of the League of Nations">League of Nations</a>, in which Haiti was also a founding member).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> In the 1950s, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourists</a> started to visit Haiti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardiantourism_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardiantourism-96">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>The waterfront area of <a href="/wiki/Port-au-Prince" title="Port-au-Prince">Port-au-Prince</a> was redeveloped to allow cruise ship passengers to walk from the docks to cultural attractions. Among these attractions were the Moorish-styled <i>Iron Market</i>, where fine <a href="/wiki/Haitian_art" title="Haitian art">Haitian art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mahogany" title="Mahogany">mahogany</a> were sold. In the evenings entrepreneurs provided dancing, casino gambling and <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Vodou" title="Haitian Vodou">Voodoo</a> shows. <a href="/wiki/Truman_Capote" title="Truman Capote">Truman Capote</a> and <a href="/wiki/No%C3%ABl_Coward" title="Noël Coward">Noël Coward</a> visited the <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Oloffson" title="Hotel Oloffson">Hotel Oloffson</a>, a 19th-century Gothic <a href="/wiki/Gingerbread_house_(architecture)" title="Gingerbread house (architecture)">gingerbread</a> mansion set in a tropical garden, which was even portrayed in the <a href="/wiki/Graham_Greene" title="Graham Greene">Graham Greene</a> novel, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Comedians_(novel)" title="The Comedians (novel)">The Comedians</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clammer.2C_Paul_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clammer.2C_Paul-97">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Duvalier_dynasty_(1957–1986)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Duvalier_dynasty_.281957.E2.80.931986.29">Duvalier dynasty (1957–1986)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Duvalier dynasty (1957–1986)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Duvalier_dynasty" title="Duvalier dynasty">Duvalier dynasty</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Duvalier_crop2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="497" data-file-width="330" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Duvalier_crop2.jpg/170px-Duvalier_crop2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Duvalier_crop2.jpg/255px-Duvalier_crop2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/98/Duvalier_crop2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Duvalier_crop2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"Papa Doc" <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Duvalier" title="François Duvalier">Duvalier</a> in 1968</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After a period of disorder, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_presidential_election,_1957" title="Haitian presidential election, 1957">September 1957</a> Dr. <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Duvalier" title="François Duvalier">François Duvalier</a> was elected President of Haiti. Known as "Papa Doc" and initially popular, Duvalier was President until his death in 1971. He advanced black interests in the public sector, where over time people of color had predominated as the educated urban elite.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bryan_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-bryan-98">[96]</a></sup> He stayed in power by enlisting an organization known as <i><a href="/wiki/Tonton_Macoute" title="Tonton Macoute">Tontons Macoutes</a></i> ("Bogeymen"), which maintained order by terrorizing the populace and political opponents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Haiti's brief tourism boom was wiped out by the rule of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francois_Duvalier" title="Francois Duvalier">Francois "Papa Doc" Duvalier</a> and his unstable government. When his son <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Duvalier" title="Jean-Claude Duvalier">Jean-Claude "Baby Doc" Duvalier</a> succeeded him as <i>President for Life</i>, tourism returned in the 1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clammer.2C_Paul_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-Clammer.2C_Paul-97">[95]</a></sup> <i>Vive la différence</i> has long been Haiti's national tourism slogan<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup> and its proximity to the United States made Haiti a hot attraction until the Duvalier regime was ousted in 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clammer.2C_Paul_97-2"><a href="#cite_note-Clammer.2C_Paul-97">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_history">Contemporary history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Contemporary history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/2004_Haitian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2004 Haitian coup d'état">2004 Haitian coup d'état</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Stabilization_Mission_in_Haiti" title="United Nations Stabilization Mission in Haiti">United Nations Stabilization Mission in Haiti</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 Haiti earthquake</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haiti_cholera_outbreak" title="Haiti cholera outbreak">Haiti cholera outbreak</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Matthew" title="Hurricane Matthew">Hurricane Matthew</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Haitian_parliamentary_election,_2015%E2%80%9316" title="Haitian parliamentary election, 2015–16">Haitian parliamentary election, 2015–16</a>; <a href="/wiki/Haitian_presidential_election,_2015" title="Haitian presidential election, 2015">Haitian presidential election, 2015</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Haitian_presidential_election,_November_2016" title="Haitian presidential election, November 2016">Haitian presidential election, November 2016</a></div>
<p>Papa Doc's son <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Duvalier" title="Jean-Claude Duvalier">Jean-Claude Duvalier</a> – also known as "Baby Doc" – led the country from 1971 until his ouster in 1986, when protests led him to seek exile in France. Army leader General <a href="/wiki/Henri_Namphy" title="Henri Namphy">Henri Namphy</a> headed a new <a href="/wiki/National_Council_of_Government_(Haiti)" title="National Council of Government (Haiti)">National Governing Council</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USEH_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-USEH-101">[99]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (July 2013)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_presidential_election,_1987" title="Haitian presidential election, 1987">General elections in November</a> were aborted after dozens of inhabitants were shot in the capital by soldiers and Tontons Macoutes. Fraudulent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_presidential_election,_1988" title="Haitian presidential election, 1988">elections followed</a>. The elected President, <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Manigat" title="Leslie Manigat">Leslie Manigat</a>, was overthrown some months later in the <a href="/wiki/June_1988_Haitian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="June 1988 Haitian coup d'état">June 1988 Haitian coup d'état</a>. The <a href="/wiki/September_1988_Haitian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="September 1988 Haitian coup d'état">September 1988 Haitian coup d'état</a>, which followed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Jean_Bosco_massacre" title="St Jean Bosco massacre">St Jean Bosco massacre</a>, revealed the increasing prominence of former Tontons Macoutes. General <a href="/wiki/Prosper_Avril" title="Prosper Avril">Prosper Avril</a> led a military regime until March 1990.</p>
<p>In December 1990, a former Catholic priest, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Bertrand_Aristide" title="Jean-Bertrand Aristide">Jean-Bertrand Aristide</a>, was elected President in the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_general_election,_1990%E2%80%9391" title="Haitian general election, 1990–91">Haitian general election</a>. In September of the following year, Aristide was overthrown by the military in the <a href="/wiki/1991_Haitian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1991 Haitian coup d'état">1991 Haitian coup d'état</a>. In 1994, an American team negotiated the departure of Haiti's military leaders and the peaceful entry of U.S. forces under <a href="/wiki/Operation_Uphold_Democracy" title="Operation Uphold Democracy">Operation Uphold Democracy</a>. This enabled the restoration of the democratically elected Jean-Bertrand Aristide as president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CCHaiti_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-CCHaiti-102">[100]</a></sup> In October 1994, Aristide returned to Haiti to complete his term in office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup> Aristide vacated the presidency in February 1996. In the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_general_election,_1995" title="Haitian general election, 1995">1995 election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Pr%C3%A9val" title="René Préval">René Préval</a> was elected as president for a five-year term, winning 88% of the popular vote.</p>
<p>In November 1994, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gordon_(1994)" title="Hurricane Gordon (1994)">Hurricane Gordon</a> brushed Haiti, dumping heavy <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">rain</a> and creating <a href="/wiki/Flash_flood" title="Flash flood">flash flooding</a> that triggered mudslides. Gordon killed an estimated 1,122 people, although some estimates go as high as 2,200.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Haitian_presidential_election,_2000" title="Haitian presidential election, 2000">November 2000 election</a> returned Aristide to the presidency with 92% of the vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup> The election had been boycotted by the opposition, then organized into the <a href="/wiki/Convergence_D%C3%A9mocratique" title="Convergence Démocratique">Convergence Démocratique</a>, over a dispute in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_legislative_election,_2000" title="Haitian legislative election, 2000">May legislative elections</a>. In subsequent years, there was increasing violence and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_rights_abuse" title="Human rights abuse">human rights abuses</a>. Aristide supporters attacked the opposition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bussandgardner_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-bussandgardner-107">[105]</a></sup> Aristide spent years negotiating with the Convergence Démocratique on new elections, but the Convergence's inability to develop a sufficient electoral base made elections unattractive.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haitian_national_palace_earthquake.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Haitian_national_palace_earthquake.jpg/300px-Haitian_national_palace_earthquake.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Haitian_national_palace_earthquake.jpg/450px-Haitian_national_palace_earthquake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Haitian_national_palace_earthquake.jpg/600px-Haitian_national_palace_earthquake.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haitian_national_palace_earthquake.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_(Haiti)" title="National Palace (Haiti)">National Palace</a> following the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 Haiti earthquake</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2004, <a href="/wiki/2004_Haitian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2004 Haitian coup d'état">a revolt began in northern Haiti</a>. The rebellion eventually reached the capital, and Aristide was forced into exile, after which the United Nations stationed peacekeepers in Haiti. Some, including Aristide and his bodyguard, Franz Gabriel, stated that he was the victim of a "new <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a> or modern kidnapping" by U.S. forces. Mrs. Aristide stated that the kidnappers wore U.S. Special Forces uniforms, but changed into civilian clothes upon boarding the aircraft that was used to remove Aristide from Haiti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Stabilisation_Mission_in_Haiti" title="United Nations Stabilisation Mission in Haiti">United Nations Stabilisation Mission (MINUSTAH)</a> was established after the 2004 coup d'état and remains in the country to the present day. <a href="/wiki/Boniface_Alexandre" title="Boniface Alexandre">Boniface Alexandre</a> assumed interim authority. <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Pr%C3%A9val" title="René Préval">René Préval</a> was elected President in February 2006, following <a href="/wiki/Haitian_general_election,_2006" title="Haitian general election, 2006">elections</a> marked by uncertainties and popular demonstrations.</p>
<p>In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jeanne#Haiti" title="Hurricane Jeanne">Tropical Storm Jeanne</a> skimmed the north coast of Haiti, leaving 3,006 people dead in flooding and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mudslide" title="Mudslide">mudslides</a>, mostly in the city of <a href="/wiki/Gona%C3%AFves" title="Gonaïves">Gonaïves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup> In 2008 Haiti was again struck by tropical storms; <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Fay_(2008)" title="Tropical Storm Fay (2008)">Tropical Storm Fay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gustav" title="Hurricane Gustav">Hurricane Gustav</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hanna" title="Hurricane Hanna">Hurricane Hanna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ike" title="Hurricane Ike">Hurricane Ike</a> all produced heavy winds and rain. There were 331 dead and about 800,000 in need of humanitarian aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup> The state of affairs produced by these storms was intensified by already high food and fuel prices that had caused a food crisis and political unrest in April 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 12 January 2010, at 4:53pm local time, Haiti was struck by a <a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale" title="Moment magnitude scale">magnitude</a>-7.0 earthquake. This was the country's most severe earthquake in over 200 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 Haiti earthquake</a> was reported to have left up to 316,000 people dead and 1.6 million homeless,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup> though later reports found these numbers to have been grossly inflated, and put the death toll between 46,000 and 85,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup> The country has yet to recover from the 2010 earthquake and a subsequent and massive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haiti_cholera_outbreak" title="Haiti cholera outbreak">Haiti cholera outbreak</a> that was triggered when cholera-infected waste from a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MINUSTAH" title="MINUSTAH">MINUSTAH</a> peacekeeping station contaminated the country's main river, the <a href="/wiki/Artibonite_River" title="Artibonite River">Artibonite</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> The country has yet to fully recover, due to both the severity of the damage Haiti endured in 2010, as well as a government that was ineffective well before the earthquake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>General elections had been planned for January 2010 but were postponed due to the earthquake. The <a href="/wiki/Haitian_general_election,_2010%E2%80%9311" title="Haitian general election, 2010–11">elections were held on 28 November 2010</a> for the senate, the parliament and the first round of the presidential elections. The run-off between <a href="/wiki/Michel_Martelly" title="Michel Martelly">Michel Martelly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mirlande_Manigat" title="Mirlande Manigat">Mirlande Manigat</a> took place on 20 March 2011, and preliminary results, released on 4 April, named Michel Martelly the winner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> On 7 February 2016, Michel Martelly stepped down as president without a successor, but only after a deal was reached for a provisional government and leaving Prime Minister Evans Paul in power "until an interim president is chosen by both chambers of Parliament."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, Haiti called for European nations to pay <a href="/wiki/Reparations_for_slavery" title="Reparations for slavery">reparations for slavery</a> and establish an official commission for the settlement of past wrongdoings. The <i>Economist</i> wrote, "Any assistance to the region should be carefully targeted; and should surely stem from today's needs, not the wrongs of the past."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> The topic, however, has more than a passing reference to a country that, as Lord Anthony Gifford wrote, "was forced to pay compensation to the government of France."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 October 2016, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Matthew" title="Hurricane Matthew">Hurricane Matthew</a> made landfall near <a href="/wiki/Les_Anglais" title="Les Anglais">Les Anglais</a>, making it the worst hurricane to strike the nation since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Cleo" title="Hurricane Cleo">Hurricane Cleo</a> in 1964. The storm brought deadly winds and rain which left Haiti with a large amount of damage to be repaired. With all of the resources in the country destroyed, Haiti received aid from the United Nations of around US$120 million. The death total was approximately 3,000. Thousands of people were displaced due to damage to infrastructure. Also, the cholera outbreak has been growing since the storm hit Haiti. With additional flooding after the storm, cholera continued to spread beyond the control of officials. The storm also caused damage to hospitals and roads which created a larger problem in helping victims and moving resources. The devastation and damage that Hurricane Matthew caused was unpredictable and left Haiti in a state of emergency.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Haiti" title="Geography of Haiti">Geography of Haiti</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haiti_topographic_map-fr.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1299" data-file-width="1739" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Haiti_topographic_map-fr.svg/350px-Haiti_topographic_map-fr.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Haiti_topographic_map-fr.svg/525px-Haiti_topographic_map-fr.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Haiti_topographic_map-fr.svg/700px-Haiti_topographic_map-fr.svg.png 2x" width="350"/></a>

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:440px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Labadee,_Haiti_from_Freedom_of_the_Seas_(13107276383)_(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5430" data-file-width="13365" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Labadee%2C_Haiti_from_Freedom_of_the_Seas_%2813107276383%29_%282%29.jpg/438px-Labadee%2C_Haiti_from_Freedom_of_the_Seas_%2813107276383%29_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Labadee%2C_Haiti_from_Freedom_of_the_Seas_%2813107276383%29_%282%29.jpg/657px-Labadee%2C_Haiti_from_Freedom_of_the_Seas_%2813107276383%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Labadee%2C_Haiti_from_Freedom_of_the_Seas_%2813107276383%29_%282%29.jpg/876px-Labadee%2C_Haiti_from_Freedom_of_the_Seas_%2813107276383%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="438"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Labadee,_Haiti_from_Freedom_of_the_Seas_(13107276383)_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Labadee" title="Labadee">Labadee</a> beach and village</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Haiti is on the western part of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>, the second largest island in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a>. Haiti is the third largest country in the Caribbean behind <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> (the latter shares a 360-kilometre (224 mi) border with Haiti). Haiti at its closest point is about 45 nautical miles (83 km; 52 mi) away from Cuba and comprises the <i>horseshoe</i>-shape peninsula and because of this, it has a disproportionately long coastline and is <i>second</i> in length (1,771 km or 1,100 mi) behind Cuba in the Greater Antilles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>Haiti is the most mountainous nation in the Caribbean and its terrain consists mainly of them interspersed with small coastal plains and river valleys. The climate is tropical, with some variation depending on altitude. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Pic_la_Selle" title="Pic la Selle">Pic la Selle</a>, at 2,680 metres (8,793 ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NgCheong-Lum.2C_Roseline_19_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-NgCheong-Lum.2C_Roseline_19-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>The northern region consists of the <i><a href="/wiki/Massif_du_Nord" title="Massif du Nord">Massif du Nord</a></i> (Northern Massif) and the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plaine_du_Nord" title="Plaine du Nord">Plaine du Nord</a></i> (Northern Plain). The <i>Massif du Nord</i> is an extension of the <i>Cordillera Central</i> in the Dominican Republic. It begins at Haiti's eastern border, north of the <a href="/wiki/Guayamouc_River" title="Guayamouc River">Guayamouc River</a>, and extends to the northwest through the northern peninsula. The lowlands of the <i>Plaine du Nord</i> lie along the northern border with the Dominican Republic, between the <i>Massif du Nord</i> and the North Atlantic Ocean.</p>
<p>The central region consists of two plains and two sets of mountain ranges. The <i>Plateau Central</i> (Central Plateau) extends along both sides of the Guayamouc River, south of the <i>Massif du Nord</i>. It runs from the southeast to the northwest. To the southwest of the <i>Plateau Central</i> are the <i>Montagnes Noires</i>, whose most northwestern part merges with the <i>Massif du Nord</i>. Its westernmost point is known as Cap Carcasse.</p>
<p>The southern region consists of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plaine_du_Cul-de-Sac" title="Plaine du Cul-de-Sac">Plaine du Cul-de-Sac</a> (the southeast) and the mountainous southern peninsula (also known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiburon_Peninsula,_Haiti" title="Tiburon Peninsula, Haiti">Tiburon Peninsula</a>). The Plaine du Cul-de-Sac is a natural depression that harbors the country's saline lakes, such as <a href="/wiki/Trou_Ca%C3%AFman" title="Trou Caïman">Trou Caïman</a> and Haiti's largest lake, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%89tang_Saumatre" title="Étang Saumatre">Étang Saumatre</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cha%C3%AEne_de_la_Selle" title="Chaîne de la Selle">Chaîne de la Selle</a> mountain range – an extension of the southern mountain chain of the Dominican Republic (the Sierra de Baoruco) – extends from the Massif de la Selle in the east to the <a href="/wiki/Massif_de_la_Hotte" title="Massif de la Hotte">Massif de la Hotte</a> in the west. This mountain range harbors <a href="/wiki/Pic_la_Selle" title="Pic la Selle">Pic la Selle</a>, the highest point in Haiti at 2,680 metres (8,793 ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (July 2013)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Haiti's most important valley in terms of crops is the Plaine de l'Artibonite, which is oriented south of the Montagnes Noires. This region supports the country's (also Hispaniola's) longest river, the <a href="/wiki/Artibonite_River" title="Artibonite River">Riviere l'Artibonite</a>, which begins in the western region of the Dominican Republic and continues most of its length through central Haiti and onward where it empties into the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Gon%C3%A2ve" title="Gulf of Gonâve">Golfe de la Gonâve</a>. The eastern and central region of the island is a large elevated plateau.</p>
<p>Haiti also includes various offshore islands. The island of <a href="/wiki/Tortuga_(Haiti)" title="Tortuga (Haiti)">Tortuga</a> (Île de la Tortue) is located off the coast of northern Haiti. The <a href="/wiki/Arrondissements_of_Haiti" title="Arrondissements of Haiti">arrondissement</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gon%C3%A2ve_Island" title="Gonâve Island">La Gonâve</a> is located on the island of the same name, in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Gon%C3%A2ve" title="Gulf of Gonâve">Golfe de la Gonâve</a>. Gonâve Island is moderately populated by rural villagers. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele_%C3%A0_Vache" title="Île à Vache">Île à Vache</a> (Cow Island), a lush island with many beautiful sights, is located off the tip of southwestern Haiti. Also part of Haiti are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cayemites" title="Cayemites">Cayemites</a> and Île d' Anacaona. <a href="/wiki/Navassa_Island" title="Navassa Island">La Navasse</a> located 40 nautical miles (46 mi; 74 km) west of <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A9r%C3%A9mie" title="Jérémie">Jérémie</a> on the south west <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a> of Haiti,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> is subject to an ongoing territorial dispute with the United States.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Haiti's climate is tropical with some variation depending on altitude. Port-au-Prince ranges in January from an average minimum of 23 °C (73.4 °F) to an average maximum of 31 °C (87.8 °F); in July, from 25–35 °C (77–95 °F). The rainfall pattern is varied, with rain heavier in some of the lowlands and the northern and eastern slopes of the mountains. Haiti's dry season occurs from November to January.</p>
<p>Port-au-Prince receives an average annual rainfall of 1,370 mm (53.9 in). There are two rainy seasons, April–June and October–November. Haiti is subject to periodic droughts and floods, made more severe by deforestation. Hurricanes are also a menace. In summary, Haiti is generally a hot and humid tropical climate.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haiti_relief_location_map.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1156" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Haiti_relief_location_map.jpg/350px-Haiti_relief_location_map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Haiti_relief_location_map.jpg/525px-Haiti_relief_location_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Haiti_relief_location_map.jpg/700px-Haiti_relief_location_map.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haiti_relief_location_map.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Haiti's topography</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are <a href="/wiki/Thrust_fault#Blind_thrust_faults" title="Thrust fault">blind thrust faults</a> associated with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enriquillo-Plantain_Garden_fault_zone" title="Enriquillo-Plantain Garden fault zone">Enriquillo-Plantain Garden fault system</a> over which Haiti lies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGSHaiti2_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-USGSHaiti2-126">[124]</a></sup> After the earthquake of 2010, there was no evidence of surface rupture and based on seismological, geological and ground deformation data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayes_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes-127">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>The northern boundary of the fault is where the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribbean_plate" title="Caribbean plate">Caribbean</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tectonic_plate" title="Tectonic plate">tectonic plate</a> shifts eastwards by about 20 mm (0.79 inches) per year in relation to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_American_plate" title="North American plate">North American plate</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strike-slip_fault" title="Strike-slip fault">strike-slip fault</a> system in the region has two branches in Haiti, the <a href="/wiki/Septentrional-Oriente_fault_zone" title="Septentrional-Oriente fault zone">Septentrional-Oriente fault</a> in the north and the Enriquillo-Plantain Garden fault in the south.</p>
<p>A 2007 earthquake hazard study, noted that the Enriquillo-Plantain Garden fault zone could be at the end of its seismic cycle and concluded that a worst-case forecast would involve a 7.2 M<sub>w</sub> earthquake, similar in size to the <a href="/wiki/1692_Jamaica_earthquake" title="1692 Jamaica earthquake">1692 Jamaica earthquake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeMets_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeMets-128">[126]</a></sup> A study team presented a hazard assessment of the Enriquillo-Plantain Garden fault system to the 18th Caribbean Geologic Conference in March 2008, noting the large strain. The team recommended "high priority" historical geologic rupture studies, as the fault was fully locked and had recorded few earthquakes in the preceding 40 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18cgc_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-18cgc-129">[127]</a></sup> An article published in Haiti's <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Matin_(Haiti)" title="Le Matin (Haiti)">Le Matin</a></i> newspaper in September 2008 cited comments by geologist Patrick Charles to the effect that there was a high risk of major seismic activity in Port-au-Prince.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lematinhaiti_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-lematinhaiti-130">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>Haiti also has rare elements such as <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">Gold</a>, which can be found at The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mont_Organis%C3%A9" title="Mont Organisé">Mont Organisé</a> <a href="/wiki/Gold_mining" title="Gold mining">gold mine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Environment_of_Haiti" title="Environment of Haiti">Environment of Haiti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Haiti" title="Deforestation in Haiti">Deforestation in Haiti</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haiti_deforestation.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Haiti_deforestation.jpg/300px-Haiti_deforestation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Haiti_deforestation.jpg/450px-Haiti_deforestation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Haiti_deforestation.jpg/600px-Haiti_deforestation.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haiti_deforestation.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Haiti's border with the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> in 2002 (right) shows the amount of deforestation on the Haitian side.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">soil erosion</a> released from the upper catchments and <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a> have caused periodic and severe flooding in Haiti, as experienced, for example, on 17 September 2004. Earlier in May that year, floods had killed over 3,000 people on Haiti's southern border with the Dominican Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>Haiti's forests covered 60 percent of the country as recently as fifty years ago, but today, according to more in-depth environmental analysis, the country yields approximately 30 percent tree cover, a stark difference from the often cited 2 percent which has been widely circulated in discourse concerning Haiti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>Scientists at the <a href="/wiki/The_Earth_Institute#Center_for_International_Earth_Science_Information_Network_.28CIESIN.29Earth_Institute" title="The Earth Institute">Columbia University's Center for International Earth Science Information Network (CIESIN)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a> are working on the Haiti Regenerative Initiative an initiative aiming to reduce poverty and natural disaster vulnerability in Haiti through ecosystem restoration and sustainable resource management.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Haiti" title="Politics of Haiti">Politics of Haiti</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haitians_voting_in_the_2006_elections.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1705" data-file-width="2598" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Haitians_voting_in_the_2006_elections.jpeg/220px-Haitians_voting_in_the_2006_elections.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Haitians_voting_in_the_2006_elections.jpeg/330px-Haitians_voting_in_the_2006_elections.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Haitians_voting_in_the_2006_elections.jpeg/440px-Haitians_voting_in_the_2006_elections.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haitians_voting_in_the_2006_elections.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Voting in the 2006 elections in <a href="/wiki/Port-au-Prince" title="Port-au-Prince">Port-au-Prince</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The government of Haiti is a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a> republic, a multiparty system wherein the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Haiti" title="President of Haiti">President of Haiti</a> is head of state elected directly by popular <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Haiti" title="Elections in Haiti">elections</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> The Prime Minister acts as head of government and is appointed by the President, chosen from the majority party in the National Assembly. Executive power is exercised by the President and Prime Minister who together constitute the government. In 2013, the annual budget was US$1 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daniel5_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-daniel5-136">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>Legislative power is vested in both the government and the two chambers of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Haiti" title="National Assembly of Haiti">National Assembly of Haiti</a>. The government is organized <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitarily</a>, thus the central government <i>delegates</i> powers to the departments without a constitutional need for consent. The current structure of Haiti's political system was set forth in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Haiti" title="Constitution of Haiti">Constitution of Haiti</a> on 29 March 1987.</p>
<p>Haitian politics have been contentious: since independence, Haiti has suffered 32 coups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup> Haiti is the only country in the Western Hemisphere to undergo a successful <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">slave revolution</a>, but a long history of oppression by dictators – including <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Duvalier" title="François Duvalier">François Duvalier</a> and his son <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Duvalier" title="Jean-Claude Duvalier">Jean-Claude Duvalier</a> – has markedly affected the nation. France, the United States and other Western countries have repeatedly intervened in Haitian politics since the country's founding, sometimes at the request of one party or another. Along with international financial institutions, they have imposed large quantities of debt – so much that foreign debt payments have rivaled the available government budget for social sector spending. There have been criticisms of financial institutions for enforcing trade policies on Haiti that are considered by some to be detrimental to local industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bell_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bell-138">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to a <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a> report in 2006, there is a strong correlation between corruption and poverty and Haiti ranked first of all countries surveyed for of levels of perceived domestic corruption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross" title="International Red Cross">International Red Cross</a> reports that seven out of ten Haitians live on less than US$2 a day, however, stated below "such statistical estimations should be looked upon very skeptically because of the fact that the average Haitian and Haitian family has to and does spend a lot more than that daily. The disconnect likely lies in the fact that these are estimates based on surveys conducted by asking individuals what their incomes are; in the Haitian culture it is very unlikely that one will receive a truthful and accurate answer to such a personal question. For various reasons individuals will not tell the truth on such a private matter. For some it is because "it's none of your business," for others, they will simply exaggerate their poor situation in hopes that some type of financial aide will be gained or rendered to them".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cit%C3%A9_Soleil" title="Cité Soleil">Cité Soleil</a> in Port-au-Prince, one of the biggest <a href="/wiki/Slum" title="Slum">slums</a> in the Northern Hemisphere, has been called "the most dangerous place on Earth" by the United Nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cit.C3.A9_Soleil_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cit.C3.A9_Soleil-141">[139]</a></sup> Many residents are supporters of former Haitian President <a href="/wiki/Jean-Bertrand_Aristide" title="Jean-Bertrand Aristide">Jean-Bertrand Aristide</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup> who, according to the BBC, "accused the US of forcing him out – an accusation the US rejected as 'absurd'".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>Jean-Bertrand Aristide was initially denied access to Haiti by Haitian immigration authorities, despite issuing appeals for entrance to his supporters and international observers. The world's most prominent governments did not overtly oppose such appeals, nor did they support them; an unnamed analyst "close to the Haitian government" quoted in several media sources –  including <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> –  is reported to have said: "Aristide could have 15 passports and he's still not going to come back to Haiti ... France and the United States are standing in the way." However, Aristide finally returned to Haiti on 18 March 2011, days before the 2011 presidential election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bel_Air,_Haiti_2008.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3072" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Bel_Air%2C_Haiti_2008.jpg/220px-Bel_Air%2C_Haiti_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Bel_Air%2C_Haiti_2008.jpg/330px-Bel_Air%2C_Haiti_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Bel_Air%2C_Haiti_2008.jpg/440px-Bel_Air%2C_Haiti_2008.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bel_Air,_Haiti_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
US Marines patrol the streets of Port-au-Prince on 14 April 2004</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first round of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_general_election,_2010" title="Haitian general election, 2010">2010 general election</a> was held in December. <a href="/wiki/Mirlande_Manigat" title="Mirlande Manigat">Mirlande Manigat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jude_C%C3%A9lestin" title="Jude Célestin">Jude Celestin</a> qualified for the second round of the presidential election, but its results were contested. Some people said that the first round was a fraud and that <a href="/wiki/Michel_Martelly" title="Michel Martelly">Michel Martelly</a> should replace Jude Celestin, René Préval's chosen successor. There was some violence between the contending parties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> On 4 April 2011, the Provisional Electoral Council announced preliminary results indicating that Martelly had won the presidential election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the U.S. funded $33 million<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup> to legislative and presidential elections in August and October 2015, a special verification panel – implemented by interim President <a href="/wiki/Jocelerme_Privert" title="Jocelerme Privert">Joceleme Privert</a> – declared the results "tainted by significant fraud".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Associated_Press_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Associated_Press-148">[146]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jovenel_Mo%C3%AFse" title="Jovenel Moïse">Jovenel Moïse</a>, the supposed winner of the October 25, 2015 election, had been hand-picked by former President <a href="/wiki/Michel_Martelly" title="Michel Martelly">Michel Martelly</a>. The month-long examination in May 2016 was created after the elections were condemned as fraudulent to restore credibility to the process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> The commission recommended completely redoing the vote after auditing a random sample of about 13,000 ballots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Associated_Press_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_Associated_Press-148">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2012, Haiti signaled it would seek to upgrade its observer status to full associate member status of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> (AU).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup> The AU was reported to be planning to upgrade Haiti's status from observer to associate at its June 2013 summit<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haitics_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-haitics-151">[149]</a></sup> but the application had still not been ratified by May 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_National_Police" title="Haitian National Police">Haitian National Police</a> force numbered 7,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup> The legal system for torts is based on a version of the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Code" title="Napoleonic Code">Napoleonic Code</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Institut_de_Sauvegarde_du_Patrimoine_National" title="Institut de Sauvegarde du Patrimoine National">Institute for the Protection of National Heritage</a> has preserved 33 historical monuments and the historic center of Cap-Haïtien.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cabinet">Cabinet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Cabinet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Haiti" title="Cabinet of Haiti">Cabinet of Haiti</a></div>
<p><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (October 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
