<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Haiti" title="Military of Haiti">Military of Haiti</a></div>
<p>Haiti's Ministry of Defense is the main body of their armed forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> The former <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Haiti" title="Armed Forces of Haiti">Haitian Armed Forces</a> were demobilized in 1995, however, <a href="/wiki/Defence_Force_of_Haiti" title="Defence Force of Haiti">efforts to reconstitute it are currently underway</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup> The current defense force for Haiti is the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_National_Police" title="Haitian National Police">Haitian National Police</a>, which has a highly trained SWAT team, and works alongside the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Coast_Guard" title="Haitian Coast Guard">Haitian Coast Guard</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement_and_crime">Law enforcement and crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Law enforcement and crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Haitian_National_Police" title="Haitian National Police">Haitian National Police</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Haiti" title="Crime in Haiti">Crime in Haiti</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fiat_Siena_DDO_--_08-11-06.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="564" data-file-width="812" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Fiat_Siena_DDO_--_08-11-06.jpg/220px-Fiat_Siena_DDO_--_08-11-06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Fiat_Siena_DDO_--_08-11-06.jpg/330px-Fiat_Siena_DDO_--_08-11-06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Fiat_Siena_DDO_--_08-11-06.jpg/440px-Fiat_Siena_DDO_--_08-11-06.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fiat_Siena_DDO_--_08-11-06.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Law enforcement in Haiti is maintained primarily by police forces for each department. The <a href="/wiki/Haitian_National_Police" title="Haitian National Police">Direction Département de L’Ouest</a> (DDO) in Port-au-Prince, is one of the six offices in the metropolitan area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Haiti has consistently ranked among the most corrupt countries in the world on the <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup> It is estimated that President <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Duvalier" title="Jean-Claude Duvalier">"Baby Doc" Duvalier</a>, his wife <a href="/wiki/Mich%C3%A8le_Bennett" title="Michèle Bennett">Michelle</a>, and their agents stole US $504 million from the country's treasury between 1971 and 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup> Similarly, after the Haitian Army folded in 1995, the Haitian National Police (HNP) gained sole power of authority on the Haitian citizens. Many Haitians as well as observers of the Haitian society believe that this monopolized power could have given way to a corrupt police force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haiti:_Police_and_Law_Enforcement_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-Haiti:_Police_and_Law_Enforcement-164">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>Similarly, some media outlets alleged that millions were stolen by former president <a href="/wiki/Jean-Bertrand_Aristide" title="Jean-Bertrand Aristide">Jean-Bertrand Aristide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-American_Spectator_Vol_1994_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-American_Spectator_Vol_1994-165">[163]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup> In March 2004, at the time of Aristide's being <a href="/wiki/Kidnapping" title="Kidnapping">kidnapped</a>, a <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> article wrote that the Bush administration State Department stated that Aristide had been involved in drug trafficking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[167]</a></sup> The BBC also described <a href="/wiki/Pyramid_scheme" title="Pyramid scheme">pyramid schemes</a>, in which Haitians lost hundreds of millions in 2002, as the "only real economic initiative" of the Aristide years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-basketcase_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-basketcase-170">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>Conversely, according to the 2013 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_on_Drugs_and_Crime" title="United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime">United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNODC" title="UNODC">UNODC</a>) report, murder rates in Haiti (10.2 per 100,000) are far <i>below</i> the regional average (26 per 100,000); less than ¼ that of Jamaica (39.3 per 100,000) and nearly ½ that of the Dominican Republic (22.1 per 100,000), making it among the safer countries in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup> In large part, this is due to the country's ability to fulfill a pledge by increasing its national police yearly by 50%, a four-year initiative that was started in 2012. In addition to the yearly recruits, the Haitian National Police (HNP) has been using innovative technologies to crack down on crime. A notable bust in recent years<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (March 2017)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> led to the dismantlement of the largest kidnapping ring in the country with the use of an advanced software program developed by a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Military_Academy" title="United States Military Academy">West Point</a>-trained Haitian official that proved to be so effective that it has led to its foreign advisers to make inquiries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Police_Department" title="New York City Police Department">New York City Police Department</a> (NYPD) sent a team of veteran officers to Haiti to assist in the rebuilding of its police force with special training in investigative techniques, strategies to improve the anti-kidnapping personnel and community outreach to build stronger relationships with the public especially among the youth. It has also helped the HNP set up a police unit in the center of <a href="/wiki/Delmas,_Ouest" title="Delmas, Ouest">Delmas</a>, a neighborhood of Port-au-Prince.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAID_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-USAID-177">[175]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012 and 2013, 150 HNP officers received specialized training funded by the US government, which also contributed to the infrastructure and communications support by upgrading radio capacity and constructing new police stations from the most violent-prone neighborhoods of <a href="/wiki/Cit%C3%A9_Soleil" title="Cité Soleil">Cité Soleil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grande_Ravine" title="Grande Ravine">Grande Ravine</a> in Port-au-Prince to the new northern industrial park at <a href="/wiki/Caracol,_Nord-Est" title="Caracol, Nord-Est">Caracol</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAID_177-1"><a href="#cite_note-USAID-177">[175]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Haiti" title="Administrative divisions of Haiti">Administrative divisions of Haiti</a></div>
<p>Administratively, Haiti is divided into ten <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Haiti" title="Departments of Haiti">departments</a>. The departments are listed below, with the departmental capital cities in parentheses.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haiti,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1057" data-file-width="1357" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Haiti%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/300px-Haiti%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Haiti%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/450px-Haiti%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Haiti%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/600px-Haiti%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haiti,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Departments of Haiti</div>
</div>
</div>
<ol>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nord-Ouest_(department)" title="Nord-Ouest (department)">Nord-Ouest</a> (<a href="/wiki/Port-de-Paix" title="Port-de-Paix">Port-de-Paix</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nord_(Haitian_department)" title="Nord (Haitian department)">Nord</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cap-Ha%C3%AFtien" title="Cap-Haïtien">Cap-Haïtien</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nord-Est_(department)" title="Nord-Est (department)">Nord-Est</a> (<a href="/wiki/Fort-Libert%C3%A9" title="Fort-Liberté">Fort-Liberté</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Artibonite_(department)" title="Artibonite (department)">Artibonite</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gona%C3%AFves" title="Gonaïves">Gonaïves</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Centre_(department)" title="Centre (department)">Centre</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hinche" title="Hinche">Hinche</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ouest_(department)" title="Ouest (department)">Ouest</a> (<a href="/wiki/Port-au-Prince" title="Port-au-Prince">Port-au-Prince</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grand%27Anse_(department)" title="Grand'Anse (department)">Grand'Anse</a> (<a href="/wiki/J%C3%A9r%C3%A9mie" title="Jérémie">Jérémie</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nippes" title="Nippes">Nippes</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mirago%C3%A2ne" title="Miragoâne">Miragoâne</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sud_(department)" title="Sud (department)">Sud</a> (<a href="/wiki/Les_Cayes" title="Les Cayes">Les Cayes</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sud-Est_(department)" title="Sud-Est (department)">Sud-Est</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jacmel" title="Jacmel">Jacmel</a>)</li>
</ol>
<p>The departments are further divided into 42 <a href="/wiki/Arrondissements_of_Haiti" title="Arrondissements of Haiti">arrondissements</a>, 145 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communes_of_Haiti" title="Communes of Haiti">communes</a> and 571 <a href="/wiki/Communal_section" title="Communal section">communal sections</a>. These serve as, respectively, second- and third-level administrative divisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Haiti" title="Economy of Haiti">Economy of Haiti</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haiti_Export_Treemap.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2085" data-file-width="2668" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Haiti_Export_Treemap.jpg/350px-Haiti_Export_Treemap.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Haiti_Export_Treemap.jpg/525px-Haiti_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Haiti_Export_Treemap.jpg/700px-Haiti_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haiti_Export_Treemap.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A proportional representation of Haiti's exports</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Haiti's <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product#Cross-border_comparison" title="Gross domestic product">purchasing power parity GDP</a> fell 8% in 2010 (from US$12.15 billion to US$11.18 billion) and the GDP per capita remained unchanged at PPP US$1,200.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_20110303_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_20110303-2">[2]</a></sup> Despite having a viable tourist industry, Haiti is one of the world's poorest countries and the poorest in the Americas region, with poverty, corruption, poor infrastructure, lack of health care and lack of education cited as the main sources. The economy receded due to the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 earthquake</a> and subsequent <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_cholera_outbreak" title="2010 Haiti cholera outbreak">outbreak of Cholera</a>. Haiti ranked 145 of 182 countries in the 2010 United Nations <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, with 57.3% of the population being deprived in at least three of the HDI's poverty measures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNDP_2010_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP_2010-181">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the disputed 2000 election and accusations about President Aristide's rule,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup> US aid to the Haitian government was cut off between 2001 and 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup> After Aristide's departure in 2004, aid was restored and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_army" title="Brazilian army">Brazilian army</a> led a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Stabilization_Mission_in_Haiti" title="United Nations Stabilization Mission in Haiti">United Nations Stabilization Mission in Haiti</a> peacekeeping operation. After almost four years of recession, the economy grew by 1.5% in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup> In September 2009, Haiti met the conditions set out by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IMF" title="IMF">IMF</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heavily_Indebted_Poor_Countries" title="Heavily Indebted Poor Countries">Heavily Indebted Poor Countries</a> program to qualify for cancellation of its external debt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup></p>
<p>More than 90 percent of the government's budget comes from an agreement with <a href="/wiki/Petrocaribe" title="Petrocaribe">Petrocaribe</a>, a Venezuela-led oil alliance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[184]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_aid">Foreign aid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Foreign aid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_aid_to_Haiti" title="Foreign aid to Haiti">Foreign aid to Haiti</a></div>
<p>Haiti received more than US$4 billion in aid from 1990 to 2003, including US$1.5 billion from the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>The largest donor is the US, followed by Canada and the European Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup> In January 2010, following the earthquake, US President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> promised US$1.15 billion in assistance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> nations pledged more than €400 million (US$616 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup></p>
<p>Neighboring <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> has also provided extensive humanitarian aid to Haiti, including the funding and construction of a public university,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[189]</a></sup> human capital, free healthcare services in the border region, and logistical support after the 2010 earthquake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[190]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the UN Office of the Special Envoy for Haiti, as of March 2012, of Humanitarian funding committed or disbursed by bilateral and multilateral donors in 2010 and 2011, only 1% has been pledged to the Haitian Government<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Port_au_Prince_after_earthquake.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Downtown_Port_au_Prince_after_earthquake.jpg/220px-Downtown_Port_au_Prince_after_earthquake.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Downtown_Port_au_Prince_after_earthquake.jpg/330px-Downtown_Port_au_Prince_after_earthquake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Downtown_Port_au_Prince_after_earthquake.jpg/440px-Downtown_Port_au_Prince_after_earthquake.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Port_au_Prince_after_earthquake.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Damage caused by the earthquake in 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the 2013 CIA World Factbook, the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 Haiti earthquake</a> inflicted an estimated US$7.8 billion in damage and caused the country's GDP to contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[192]</a></sup></p>
<p>The United Nations states that in total US$13.34 billion has been earmarked for the crisis through 2020, though two years after the 2010 quake, less than half of that amount had actually been released, according to UN documents. As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the US government has allocated US$4 billion; US$3 billion has already been spent, and the rest is dedicated to longer-term projects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup></p>
<p>Former US President Bill Clinton's foundation contributed US$250,000 to a <a href="/wiki/Recycling" title="Recycling">recycling</a> initiative for a sister-program of "Ranmase Lajan" or "Picking Up Money" by use of <a href="/wiki/Reverse_vending_machine" title="Reverse vending machine">reverse vending machines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[194]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trade">Trade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Trade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the 2015 CIA <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Factbook" title="World Factbook">World Factbook</a>, Haiti's main import partners are: Dominican Republic 35%, US 26.8%, Netherlands Antilles 8.7%, China 7% (est. 2013). Haiti's main export partner is the US 83.5% (est. 2013).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup></p>
<p>Haiti had a trade deficit of US$3 billion in 2011, or 41% of GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ammart_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-ammart-198">[196]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1925, the city of Jacmel was the first area in the Caribbean to have electricity and was subsequently dubbed the <i>City of Light</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>Today, Haiti relies heavily on an oil alliance with <a href="/wiki/Petrocaribe" title="Petrocaribe">Petrocaribe</a> for much of its energy requirements. In recent years, hydroelectric, solar and wind energy have been explored as possible sustainable energy sources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[198]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_income">Personal income</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Personal income">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CapHaitienMarche.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1189" data-file-width="1771" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/CapHaitienMarche.jpg/300px-CapHaitienMarche.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/CapHaitienMarche.jpg/450px-CapHaitienMarche.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/CapHaitienMarche.jpg/600px-CapHaitienMarche.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CapHaitienMarche.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A market in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cap_Haitien" title="Cap Haitien">Cap Haitien</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">The World Factbook</a></i> reports a shortage of skilled labor, widespread unemployment and underemployment, saying "more than two-thirds of the labor force do not have formal jobs." It is also often stated that three-quarters of the population lives on US$2 or less per day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-201">[199]</a></sup> Such statistical estimations could be viewed with skepticism because the average Haitian and Haitian family spends more than that daily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_201-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-201">[199]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">The World Factbook</a></i> also states that "remittances are the primary source of foreign exchange, equaling one-fifth (20%) of GDP and representing more than five times the earnings from exports in 2012".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[200]</a></sup> This implies that <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a> are the life-blood of the Haitian economy.</p>
<p>The World Bank estimates that over 80% of college graduates from Haiti were living abroad in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[201]</a></sup></p>
<p>Haiti's economy was severely impacted by the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 Haiti earthquake</a> which occurred on 12 January 2010, killing over 300,000 and displacing 1.5 million residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-204">[202]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Real_estate">Real estate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Real estate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In rural areas, people often live in wooden huts with corrugated iron roofs. Outhouses are located in back of the huts. In Port-au-Prince, colorful <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shantytowns" title="Shantytowns">shantytowns</a> surround the central city and go up the mountainsides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-c151222_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-c151222-205">[203]</a></sup></p>
<p>The middle and upper classes live in Suburbs, or in the central part of the bigger cities in apartments, where there is urban planning. Many of the houses they live in are like miniature fortresses, located behind walls embedded with metal spikes, barbed wire, broken glass, and sometimes all three. The gates to these houses are barred at night, the house is locked; guard dogs patrol the yard. These houses are often self-sufficient as well. The houses have backup generators, because the electrical grid in Haiti is unreliable. Some even have rooftop reservoirs for water, as the water supply is also unreliable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-c151222_205-1"><a href="#cite_note-c151222-205">[203]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Haiti" title="Agriculture in Haiti">Agriculture in Haiti</a></div>
<p>Haiti is the world's leading producer of <a href="/wiki/Chrysopogon_zizanioides" title="Chrysopogon zizanioides">vetiver</a>, a root plant used to make luxury perfumes, essential oils and fragrances, providing for half the world's supply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[206]</a></sup> Half of all Haitians work in the agricultural sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-feedh_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-feedh-209">[207]</a></sup> Haiti relies upon imports for half its food needs and 80% of its rice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-feedh_209-1"><a href="#cite_note-feedh-209">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>Haiti exports crops such as <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mangoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cacao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papaya" title="Papaya">papayas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahogany" title="Mahogany">mahogany</a> nuts, <a href="/wiki/Spinach" title="Spinach">spinach</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Watercress" title="Watercress">watercress</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ute.gouv.ht_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-ute.gouv.ht-210">[208]</a></sup> Agricultural products comprise 6% of all exports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ammart_198-1"><a href="#cite_note-ammart-198">[196]</a></sup> In addition, local agricultural products include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corn" title="Corn">corn</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beans" title="Beans">beans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potato</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">peanuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pistachio" title="Pistachio">pistachios</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pigeon_pea" title="Pigeon pea">pigeon peas</a>, sugarcane, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wood" title="Wood">wood</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ute.gouv.ht_210-1"><a href="#cite_note-ute.gouv.ht-210">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[209]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Currency">Currency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Currency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Haitian_gourde" title="Haitian gourde">Haitian gourde</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Haitian_gourde" title="Haitian gourde">Haitian gourde</a> (HTG) is the national currency. The "<a href="/wiki/Haitian_gourde" title="Haitian gourde">Haitian dollar</a>" equates to 5 gourdes (<i>goud</i>), which is a fixed exchange rate that exists in concept <i>only,</i> but are commonly used as informal prices.</p>
<p>The vast majority of the business sector and individuals in Haiti will also accept US dollars, though at the outdoor markets gourdes may be preferred. Locals may refer to the USD as "dollar américain" (<i>dola ameriken</i>) or "dollar US" (pronounced <i>oos</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[210]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Haiti" title="Tourism in Haiti">Tourism in Haiti</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jacmel_Seaside.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="468" data-file-width="960" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Jacmel_Seaside.jpg/300px-Jacmel_Seaside.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Jacmel_Seaside.jpg/450px-Jacmel_Seaside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Jacmel_Seaside.jpg/600px-Jacmel_Seaside.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jacmel_Seaside.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Seaside in <a href="/wiki/Jacmel" title="Jacmel">Jacmel</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Labadee.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1011" data-file-width="2244" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Labadee.jpg/300px-Labadee.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Labadee.jpg/450px-Labadee.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Labadee.jpg/600px-Labadee.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Labadee.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Labadee" title="Labadee">Labadee</a>, a cruise ship destination</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2014, the country received 1,250,000 tourists (mostly from cruise ships), and the industry generated US$200 million in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daniel5_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-daniel5-136">[134]</a></sup> In December 2014, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_State_Department" title="US State Department">US State Department</a> issued a travel warning about the country, noting that while thousands of American citizens safely visit Haiti each year, a few foreign tourists had been victims of burglary, predominantly in the <a href="/wiki/Port-au-Prince" title="Port-au-Prince">Port-au-Prince</a> area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bcawarn_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-bcawarn-213">[211]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several hotels were opened in 2014, including an upscale <a href="/wiki/Best_Western#Differentiation" title="Best Western">Best Western Premier</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[212]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[213]</a></sup> a five-star Royal Oasis hotel by Occidental Hotel and Resorts in <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A9tion-Ville" title="Pétion-Ville">Pétion-Ville</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[214]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[215]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[216]</a></sup> a four-star <a href="/wiki/Marriott_International" title="Marriott International">Marriott</a> hotel in the Turgeau area of Port-au-Prince<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[217]</a></sup> and other new hotel developments in Port-au-Prince, <a href="/wiki/Les_Cayes" title="Les Cayes">Les Cayes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cap-Ha%C3%AFtien" title="Cap-Haïtien">Cap-Haïtien</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jacmel" title="Jacmel">Jacmel</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Other tourist destinations include <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele-%C3%A0-Vache" title="Île-à-Vache">Île-à-Vache</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camp-Perrin" title="Camp-Perrin">Camp-Perrin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pic_Macaya" title="Pic Macaya">Pic Macaya</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Carnival" title="Haitian Carnival">Haitian Carnival</a> has been one of the most popular carnivals in the Caribbean. In 2010, the government decided to stage the event in a different city outside Port-au-Prince every year in an attempt to decentralize the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haitilibre.com_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-haitilibre.com-220">[218]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[219]</a></sup> The National Carnival –  usually held in one of the country's largest cities (i.e., Port-au-Prince, Cap-Haïtien or Les Cayes) –  follows the also very popular Jacmel Carnival, which takes place a week earlier in February or March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haitilibre.com_220-1"><a href="#cite_note-haitilibre.com-220">[218]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Caracol_Industrial_Park">Caracol Industrial Park</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Caracol Industrial Park">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 21 October 2012, Haitian President <a href="/wiki/Michel_Martelly" title="Michel Martelly">Michel Martelly</a>, US Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>, Bill Clinton, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ben_Stiller" title="Ben Stiller">Ben Stiller</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sean_Penn" title="Sean Penn">Sean Penn</a> inaugurated the 600 acres (240 ha) Caracol industrial park, the largest in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday.com_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday.com-222">[220]</a></sup> Costing US$300 million, the project, which includes a 10-megawatt <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_plant" title="Power plant">power plant</a>, a water-treatment plant and worker housing, is intended to transform the northern part of the country by creating 65,000 jobs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday.com_222-1"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday.com-222">[220]</a></sup></p>
<p>The park is part of a "master plan" for Haiti's North and North-East departments, including the expansion of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cap-Haitien_International_Airport" title="Cap-Haitien International Airport">Cap-Haitien International Airport</a> to accommodate large international flights, the construction of an international Seaport in <a href="/wiki/Fort-Libert%C3%A9" title="Fort-Liberté">Fort-Liberté</a> and the opening of the $50 million Roi Henri Christophe Campus of a new university in Limonade (near Cap-Haitien) on 12 January 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[221]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korean</a> clothing manufacturer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sae-A_Trading_Co._Ltd" title="Sae-A Trading Co. Ltd">Sae-A Trading Co. Ltd</a>, one of the park's main tenants, has created 5,000 permanent jobs out of the 20,000 projected and has built 8,600 houses in the surrounding area for its workers. The industrial park ultimately has the potential to create as many as 65,000 jobs once fully developed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[222]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[223]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Haiti" title="Transport in Haiti">Transport in Haiti</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haiti_rail_map_1925.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="580" data-file-width="779" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Haiti_rail_map_1925.jpg/300px-Haiti_rail_map_1925.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Haiti_rail_map_1925.jpg/450px-Haiti_rail_map_1925.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Haiti_rail_map_1925.jpg/600px-Haiti_rail_map_1925.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haiti_rail_map_1925.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rail map as of 1925</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Haiti has two main highways that run from one end of the country to the other. The northern highway, Route Nationale No. 1 (National Highway One), originates in Port-au-Prince, winding through the coastal towns of <a href="/wiki/Montrouis" title="Montrouis">Montrouis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gona%C3%AFves" title="Gonaïves">Gonaïves</a>, before reaching its terminus at the northern port <a href="/wiki/Cap-Ha%C3%AFtien" title="Cap-Haïtien">Cap-Haïtien</a>. The southern highway, Route Nationale No. 2, links Port-au-Prince with <a href="/wiki/Les_Cayes" title="Les Cayes">Les Cayes</a> via <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9og%C3%A2ne" title="Léogâne">Léogâne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petit-Go%C3%A2ve" title="Petit-Goâve">Petit-Goâve</a>.</p>
<p>According to the Washington Post, "Officials from the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers said Saturday [23 January 2010] that they assessed the damage from the [12 January] quake in Port-au-Prince, Haiti, and found that many of the roads aren't any worse than they were before because they've always been in poor condition."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[224]</a></sup></p>
<p>The port at Port-au-Prince, <a href="/wiki/Port_international_de_Port-au-Prince" title="Port international de Port-au-Prince">Port international de Port-au-Prince</a>, has more registered shipping than any of the other dozen ports in the country. The port's facilities include <a href="/wiki/Crane_(machine)" title="Crane (machine)">cranes</a>, large <a href="/wiki/Berth_(moorings)" title="Berth (moorings)">berths</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Warehouse" title="Warehouse">warehouses</a>, but these facilities are not in good condition. The port is underused, possibly due to the substantially high port fees. The port of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Marc" title="Saint-Marc">Saint-Marc</a> is currently the preferred port of entry for consumer goods coming into Haiti. Reasons for this may include its location away from volatile and <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">congested</a> Port-au-Prince, as well as its central location relative to numerous Haitian cities.</p>
<p>During the 2010 earthquake, the Port-au-Prince port suffered widespread damage, impeding aid to the victims. The main pier caved in and fell into the water. One of the main cranes also collapsed in the water. Port access roads were severely damaged as well.</p>
<p>In the past, Haiti used rail transport, however the rail infrastructure was poorly maintained when in use and cost of rehabilitation is beyond the means of the Haitian economy.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toussaint_Louverture_International_Airport.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1940" data-file-width="3373" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Toussaint_Louverture_International_Airport.jpg/220px-Toussaint_Louverture_International_Airport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Toussaint_Louverture_International_Airport.jpg/330px-Toussaint_Louverture_International_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Toussaint_Louverture_International_Airport.jpg/440px-Toussaint_Louverture_International_Airport.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toussaint_Louverture_International_Airport.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Toussaint L'Ouverture International Airport</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Haiti" title="List of airports in Haiti">List of airports in Haiti</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Toussaint_Louverture_International_Airport" title="Toussaint Louverture International Airport">Toussaint Louverture International Airport</a>, located 10 kilometres (6.2 mi) North/North East of Port-au-Prince proper in the commune of <a href="/wiki/Tabarre" title="Tabarre">Tabarre</a>, is the primary transportation hub regarding entry and exit into the country. It has Haiti's main <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jetway" title="Jetway">jetway</a>, and along with <a href="/wiki/Cap-Ha%C3%AFtien_International_Airport" title="Cap-Haïtien International Airport">Cap-Haïtien International Airport</a> located near the northern city of Cap-Haïtien, handles the vast majority of the country's international flights. Cities such as Jacmel, Jérémie, Les Cayes, and Port-de-Paix have smaller, less accessible airports that are serviced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regional_airlines" title="Regional airlines">regional airlines</a> and private aircraft. Such companies include: <a href="/wiki/Caribintair" title="Caribintair">Caribintair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunrise_Airways" title="Sunrise Airways">Sunrise Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tortug%27_Air" title="Tortug' Air">Tortug' Air</a>.</p>
<p>In 2013, plans for the development of an international airport on Île-à-Vache were introduced by the Prime Minister.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[225]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus_service">Bus service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Bus service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tap_tap_public_transportation_Haiti.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="431" data-file-width="800" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Tap_tap_public_transportation_Haiti.jpg/220px-Tap_tap_public_transportation_Haiti.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Tap_tap_public_transportation_Haiti.jpg/330px-Tap_tap_public_transportation_Haiti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Tap_tap_public_transportation_Haiti.jpg/440px-Tap_tap_public_transportation_Haiti.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tap_tap_public_transportation_Haiti.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A "Tap tap" bus in <a href="/wiki/Port-Salut" title="Port-Salut">Port-Salut</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tap_tap" title="Tap tap">Tap tap</a> buses are colorfully painted buses or pick-up trucks that serve as share taxis. The "tap tap" name comes from the sound of passengers tapping on the metal bus body to indicate they want off.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[226]</a></sup> These vehicles for hire are often privately owned and extensively decorated. They follow fixed routes, do not leave until filled with passengers, and riders can usually disembark at any point. The decorations are a typically Haitian form of art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[227]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2013, the first coach bus prototype was made in Haiti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-http_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-http-230">[228]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Haiti" title="Telecommunications in Haiti">Telecommunications in Haiti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Haiti" title="Television in Haiti">Television in Haiti</a></div>
<p>In Haiti, communications include the radio, television, fixed and mobile telephones, and the Internet. Haiti ranked last among North American countries in the World Economic Forum's Network Readiness Index (NRI) –  an indicator for determining the development level of a country's information and communication technologies. Haiti ranked number 143 out of 148 overall in the 2014 NRI ranking, down from 141 in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[229]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Water supply and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Haiti" title="Water supply and sanitation in Haiti">Water supply and sanitation in Haiti</a></div>
<p>Haiti faces key challenges in the <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">water supply</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a> sector: Notably, access to public services is very low, their quality is inadequate and public institutions remain very weak despite foreign aid and the government's declared intent to strengthen the sector's institutions. Foreign and Haitian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NGO" title="NGO">NGOs</a> play an important role in the sector, especially in rural and urban slum areas.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Haiti" title="Demographics of Haiti">Demographics of Haiti</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haiti-demographie.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="725" height="264" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Haiti-demographie.png/450px-Haiti-demographie.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Haiti-demographie.png/675px-Haiti-demographie.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8e/Haiti-demographie.png 2x" width="450"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haiti-demographie.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Haiti's population (1961–2003)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Haiti's population was about 10.8 million according to UN 2016 estimates,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">[3]</a></sup> with half of the population younger than age 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[230]</a></sup> In 1950 the first formal census gave a total population of 3.1 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[231]</a></sup> Haiti averages approximately 350 people per square kilometer (~900 per sq mi.), with its population is concentrated most heavily in urban areas, coastal plains, and valleys.</p>
<p>Most modern Haitians are descendants of former black <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Africa" title="Ethnic groups of Africa">African</a> slaves, including <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">Mulattoes</a> who are <a href="/wiki/Multiracial" title="Multiracial">mixed-race</a>. The remainder are of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> descent and <a href="/wiki/Arab_Haitians" title="Arab Haitians">Arab Haitians</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-joshuaproject.net_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-joshuaproject.net-234">[232]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[233]</a></sup> the descendants of settlers (colonial remnants and contemporary immigration during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">WWI</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">WWII</a>). Haitians of <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asian</a> descent or <a href="/wiki/Marabou_(ethnicity)" title="Marabou (ethnicity)">East Indian</a> origin number approximately 400+.</p>
<p>Millions of Haitians live abroad in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (primarily <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Antilles" title="French Antilles">French Antilles</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos" title="Turks and Caicos">Turks and Caicos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>. There are an estimated 881,500 in the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[234]</a></sup> 800,000 in the Dominican Republic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pinadep_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-pinadep-237">[235]</a></sup> 300,000 in Cuba,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[236]</a></sup> 100,000 in Canada,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[237]</a></sup> 80,000 in France,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[238]</a></sup> and up to 80,000 in the Bahamas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[239]</a></sup> There are also smaller Haitian communities in many other countries, including <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>.</p>
<p>In 2015, the life expectancy at birth was 63 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[240]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_genetics">Population genetics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Population genetics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Autosomal_DNA">Autosomal DNA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Autosomal DNA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Gene_pool" title="Gene pool">gene pool</a> of Haiti is about 95.5% <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan African</a>, 4.3% <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European</a>, with the rest showing some traces of <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asian</a> genes;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-243">[241]</a></sup> according to a 2010 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autosomal" title="Autosomal">autosomal</a> <a href="/wiki/Genealogical_DNA_test" title="Genealogical DNA test">genealogical DNA testing</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Y-chromosome_and_Mitochondrial_DNA">Y-chromosome and Mitochondrial DNA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Y-chromosome and Mitochondrial DNA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="31" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/44px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/66px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/88px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="44"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b> with: information about <a href="/wiki/Human_mitochondrial_DNA_haplogroup" title="Human mitochondrial DNA haplogroup">Human mitochondrial DNA haplogroups</a>, which assesses the DNA inherited by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matriline" title="Matriline">matriline</a>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(June 2015)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A 2012 genetic study on Haitian and Jamaican <a href="/wiki/Human_Y-chromosome_DNA_haplogroup" title="Human Y-chromosome DNA haplogroup">Y-chromosomal ancestry</a>, has revealed that both populations "exhibit a predominantly <a href="/wiki/Y-DNA_haplogroups_in_populations_of_Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Y-DNA haplogroups in populations of Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan paternal component</a>, with haplogroups <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_A_(Y-DNA)" title="Haplogroup A (Y-DNA)">A1b-V152</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_A_(Y-DNA)" title="Haplogroup A (Y-DNA)">A3-M32</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haplogroup_B_(Y-DNA)" title="Haplogroup B (Y-DNA)">B2-M182</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haplogroup_E_(Y-DNA)" title="Haplogroup E (Y-DNA)">E1a-M33</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haplogroup_E_(Y-DNA)" title="Haplogroup E (Y-DNA)">E1b1a-M2</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haplogroup_E_(Y-DNA)" title="Haplogroup E (Y-DNA)">E2b-M98</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haplogroup_R1b_(Y-DNA)#R1b1c_.28R-V88.29" title="Haplogroup R1b (Y-DNA)">R1b2-V88</a>" comprising (77.2%) of the Haitian and (66.7%) of Jamaican paternal gene pools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-244">[242]</a></sup> Y Chromosomes indicative of <a href="/wiki/Y-DNA_haplogroups_in_populations_of_Europe" title="Y-DNA haplogroups in populations of Europe">European ancestry</a> "(i.e., haplogroups <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_G-M201" title="Haplogroup G-M201">G2a*-P15</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_I-M170" title="Haplogroup I-M170">I-M258</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haplogroup_R1b_(Y-DNA)#R1b1a2_.28R-M269.29" title="Haplogroup R1b (Y-DNA)">R1b1b-M269</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_T-M184" title="Haplogroup T-M184">T-M184</a>) were detected at commensurate levels in Haiti (20.3%) and Jamaica (18.9%)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_244-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-244">[242]</a></sup> This corresponds to approximately 1 in every 5 Paternal ancestors, hailing from Europe. While, Y-haplogroups indicative of Chinese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/O-M175" title="O-M175">O-M175</a> (3.8%) and Indian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/H-M69" title="H-M69">H-M69</a> (0.6%) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L-M20" title="L-M20">L-M20</a> (0.6%) ancestry were found at significant levels in Jamaica,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_244-2"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-244">[242]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_Haitian" title="Arab Haitian">Levantine</a> Y-haplogroups were found in Haiti.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Duffy_antigens">Duffy antigens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Duffy antigens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>According to a 2008 study examining the frequency of the <a href="/wiki/Duffy_antigen_system" title="Duffy antigen system">Duffy antigen</a> receptor for <a href="/wiki/Chemokine" title="Chemokine">Chemokines</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DARC_(gene)" title="DARC (gene)">DARC</a>) <a href="/wiki/Single-nucleotide_polymorphism" title="Single-nucleotide polymorphism">Single Nucleotide polymorphisms</a> (SNPs), (75%) of Haitian women sampled exhibited the CC genotype (absent among women of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> ancestry) at levels comparable to US <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African-Americans" title="African-Americans">African-Americans</a> (73%), but more than <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaican</a> females (63%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Genetic-structure_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-Genetic-structure-245">[243]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[244]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Casta_discrimination">Casta discrimination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Casta discrimination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Casta" title="Casta">Casta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gens_de_couleur" title="Gens de couleur">Gens de couleur</a></div>
<p>Due to the <a href="/wiki/Casta" title="Casta">racial caste system</a> instituted in colonial Haiti, <a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">Haitian mulattoes</a> became the nation's social elite and racially privileged. Numerous leaders throughout Haiti's history have been mulattoes. Comprising 5% of the nation's population, mulattoes have retained their preeminence, evident in the political, economic, social and cultural hierarchy in Haiti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[245]</a></sup> During this time, the slaves and the affranchis were given limited opportunities toward education, income, and occupations, but even after gaining independence, the social structure remains a legacy today as the disparity between the upper and lower classes have not been reformed significantly since the colonial days. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[246]</a></sup> As a result, the elite class today consists of a small group of influential people who are generally light in color and continue to establish themselves in high, prestigious positions. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[247]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_P%C3%A9tion" title="Alexandre Pétion">Alexandre Pétion</a>, born to a Haitian mother and a wealthy French father, was the first President of the Republic of Haiti.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Haiti" title="Religion in Haiti">Religion in Haiti</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">
<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden">

</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Religion in Haiti according to the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> (2010)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[248]</a></sup></p>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:purple; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Catholicism (56.8%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Blue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Protestantism (29.6%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:gray; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Unaffiliated (10.6%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Red; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Other (3%)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 2017 CIA Factbook reported that around 54.7% of Haitians profess to being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Haiti" title="Roman Catholicism in Haiti">Catholics</a> while <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Haiti" title="Protestantism in Haiti">Protestants</a> made up about 28.5% of the population (Baptist 15.4%, Pentecostal 7.9%, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist" title="Seventh-day Adventist">Seventh-day Adventist</a> 3%, Methodist 1.5%, other 0.7%). Other sources put the Protestant population higher than this, suggesting that it might have formed one-third of the population in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReyStepick2013_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReyStepick2013-251">[249]</a></sup> Moreover, Haiti is affected by a common Latin American phenomenon, i.e. a Protestant expansion, which is largely <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelical_Protestant" title="Evangelical Protestant">Evangelical Protestant</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a> in nature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[250]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[251]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[252]</a></sup> Haitian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardinal_(Catholicism)" title="Cardinal (Catholicism)">Cardinal</a> <a href="/wiki/Chibly_Langlois" title="Chibly Langlois">Chibly Langlois</a> is president of the National Bishops Conference of the Catholic Church.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_vodou" title="Haitian vodou">Vodou</a>, a religion with African roots similar to those of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, originated during colonial times in which slaves were obliged to disguise their <a href="/wiki/Loa" title="Loa">loa</a> or spirits as <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> saints, an element of a process called <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretism</a> and is still practiced by some Haitians today. Since the religious syncretism between Catholicism and Vodou, it is difficult to estimate the number of Vodouists in Haiti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[253]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[254]</a></sup></p>
<p>Minority religions in Haiti include <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Haiti" title="Islam in Haiti">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_in_Haiti" title="Bahá'í Faith in Haiti">Bahá'í Faith</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Haiti" title="History of the Jews in Haiti">Judaism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_20110303_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_20110303-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The two official languages of Haiti are <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole" title="Haitian Creole">Haitian Creole</a>. French is the principal written and administratively authorized language (as well as the main language of the press) and is spoken by 42% of Haitians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[255]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[256]</a></sup> It is spoken by all educated Haitians, is the medium of instruction in most schools, and is used in the business sector. It is also used in ceremonial events such as weddings, graduations and church masses. Haiti is one of two independent nations in the Americas (along with Canada) to designate French as an <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>; the other French-speaking areas are all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_overseas_departments_and_territories" title="French overseas departments and territories">overseas</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Departments_of_France" title="Departments of France">départements</a></i>, or <i><a href="/wiki/Overseas_collectivity" title="Overseas collectivity">collectivités</a>,</i> of France.</p>
<p>Haitian Creole,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[257]</a></sup> which has recently undergone a standardization, is spoken by virtually the entire population of Haiti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[258]</a></sup> Haitian Creole is one of the <a href="/wiki/French-based_creole_languages" title="French-based creole languages">French-based creole languages</a>. Its vocabulary is 90% derived from French, but its grammar resembles that of some West African languages. It also has influences from Taino, Spanish, and Portuguese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[259]</a></sup> Haitian Creole is related to the other <a href="/wiki/French-based_creole_languages" title="French-based creole languages">French creoles</a>, but most closely to the <a href="/wiki/Antillean_Creole" title="Antillean Creole">Antillean Creole</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louisiana_Creole_French" title="Louisiana Creole French">Louisiana Creole</a> variants.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emigration">Emigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Haiti&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Emigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Haitian_diaspora" title="Haitian diaspora">Haitian diaspora</a></div>
<p>Emigrants from Haiti have constituted a segment of American and Canadian society since before <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">the independence of Haiti from France</a> in 1804.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HammondCanadaHaiti2010_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-HammondCanadaHaiti2010-262">[260]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBSResourceBank_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-PBSResourceBank-263">[261]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many influential early American settlers and black freemen, including <a href="/wiki/Jean_Baptiste_Point_du_Sable" title="Jean Baptiste Point du Sable">Jean Baptiste Point du Sable</a> and <a href="/wiki/W._E._B._Du_Bois" title="W. E. B. Du Bois">W. E. B. Du Bois</a>, were of Haitian origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kinzie_1856_190_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kinzie_1856_190-264">[262]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Meehan_1963_445_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-Meehan_1963_445-265">[263]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cohn2009_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cohn2009-266">[264]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis18_267-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis18-267">[265]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jean_Baptiste_Point_du_Sable" title="Jean Baptiste Point du Sable">Jean Baptiste Point du Sable</a>, an immigrant from <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a> (now the Republic of Haiti), founded the first nonindigenous settlement in what is now <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois" title="Chicago, Illinois">Chicago, Illinois</a>, the third largest city in the United States. The state of Illinois and city of Chicago declared du Sable the founder of Chicago on 26 October 1968.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kinzie_1856_190_264-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kinzie_1856_190-264">[262]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Meehan_1963_445_265-1"><a href="#cite_note-Meehan_1963_445-265">[263]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cohn2009_266-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cohn2009-266">[264]</a></sup></p>
